From the Quanzhou Prefecture of Fujian, Another Communist Institution Uncovered 69

Capture of Seven Key Bandits, Yin Lidong Escapes

Xiamen Communication: In early April of this year, after the entire communist organization and maritime network of Xiamen Central City were dismantled, from late April to May 4th, the Anxi Anti-Communist Volunteers of the 26th Brigade of the 9th Division further dismantled the central hub of Anxi, Nan'an, and Jinjiang under Quanzhou Prefecture. On the 6th, the brigade headquarters issued the following report: After the leader of the pseudo-Liancheng District group, Peng Degui, the political instructor of the central county committee of An'nan Yongde, slipped into the vicinity of the city temple while our army was suppressing bandits in the third and fourth districts of Anxi, he gathered disillusioned local militias. In less than a month, it had become the First District of Anxi, with over 300 party members, over 600 civilians, and possessing over ten rifles and short guns. Due to the diligent suppression by Wang Lichun, Chen Jiang, Chen Shuxing, and others, except for the bandit Peng, Ye Che, Zeng Kui, and Li Jingwen who fled to southern Jinjiang, all personnel and weapons were resolved. Most of the civilians came from self-rehabilitation. Bandit Peng entered Jinjiang and Nan'an to provide assistance, forming a pseudo-organization in southern Jinjiang. On April 19th, the team, led by Wang Lichun, a rehabilitated individual, spent six days searching the area of southern Jinjiang, uncovering the location of bandit Peng and his main institution in Nan'an's Hehe. On the night of the 27th, they surrounded and attempted to capture bandit Peng in the area of Xidong, but he broke through and escaped. The next day, they captured Ye Che, the pseudo-reserve team leader, who confessed that Peng had been fatally wounded by bullets, causing widespread panic among the pseudo-party in southern Jinjiang. Over three days, they also captured Old Li, a highly effective reward recipient from the Li Lisan era, Chen Xiulan, a former worker at the pseudo-party headquarters of An'nan Yong, and Old Xie, a former pseudo-party military doctor from An'nan Yong, among others. On May 4th, they further uncovered the pseudo-central institution in Hehe. Yin Lidong, a key bandit leader from Quanzhou, escaped. They captured Lao Cai, an executive committee member of the pseudo-Southern Fujian Special Committee and leader of the guerrilla brigade, Xiao Fu, the propaganda chief of the pseudo-Southern Fujian Special Committee, and Cai She, the pseudo-reserve team leader of Jin Tao, Nan'an, among others. Investigations revealed that the local communists between Quanzhou and Yongchun were recently contemplating renewed activities, with Yin Lidong and Lao Cai as the masterminds, and Peng Deqing, Xiao Fu, and Cai She attached to them. Now that five bandits are either dead or captured, only Yin Lidong remains, who is now completely isolated. (May 7th)

Random Notes from the Hubei Countryside 70

(Special Correspondent for This Newspaper, Cheng Jun) (9) Examination of the Daye Mining Area

Daye's mineral wealth is unmatched in the entire province. Gold, silver, copper, iron, manganese, nickel, tin, coal, and various other minerals are certainly produced, and all should be available. In addition to the gold mine in Jinshan Temple, the silver mine in Longjiao Mountain, the manganese mine in Baiyanglin, and the mica in Lingzi Mountain, iron, coal, lime, and cement are being separately mined and manufactured. Mining companies are numerous, employing a large number of workers, and have a significant impact on the countryside. In recent years, Yangxin and Daye counties have suffered successive disasters, with the rural areas of Yangxin completely bankrupt, while the people of Daye have been spared death. The suffering is the same, but the outcome is different, which can undoubtedly be attributed to the employment opportunities provided by the various mines. The largest mines include the Hanyeping Iron Works, the Xiangbishan Iron Mine, the Fuyuan, Fuhua, and Lihua coal mines, and the Huaji Cement Factory. The Xiang Mine is government-run, while the rest are privately run. Due to external treaty restrictions or sluggish sales, they are declining daily, all facing an uncertain future. There are more than twenty smaller coal mines, such as Fudong, Yuli, Huaxing, Fuchun, Siwei, Yue, Dehe, and Housheng mines, which are either still operating or have already closed down, and are even less worthy of mention. To understand the actual situation of each mine, the reporter traveled from Daye County to Shihuiyao on April 5th, spending four days visiting almost all the major mines and factories, gaining a great deal of information, which is detailed below:

Hanyeping Iron Mine 71

The iron mine mined by Hanyeping Company was discovered in the second year of Guangxu's reign in the late Qing dynasty when Sheng Xuanhuai hired a British mining engineer to identify the geology and ore deposits. The mining area stretches hundreds of miles, and its reserves are estimated by German engineer Reulen to be at least 30 million tons. In the sixteenth year of Guangxu, Zhang Wenxiang, the Governor-General of Huguang, recognized the importance of industry and began government-led operations. Mining began in the same year, but due to objections from the Ministry of Revenue, it was changed to commercial operations in the twenty-second year. Records of iron production began at this time. In the thirty-fourth year, it merged with the Pingxiang Coal Mine and the Hanyang Iron Works, using the iron ore produced and the Pingxiang coking coal to smelt iron in the Hanyang Iron Works. The so-called Hanyeping Company included the coal from Pingxiang, the iron from Daye, and the ironworks from Hanyang. Later, due to the inconvenience of transporting iron ore to Hanyang, a furnace was built in Shihuiyao to smelt iron. Construction began in 1915 and was completed in 1919, but smelting has long been discontinued. However, iron ore mining continues.

The mining area is divided into two sections: Laotieshan and Dedao Bay. The Laotieshan section is divided into Tiemenkan and Shamaochi. Tiemenkan uses open-pit mining, while Shamaochi has tunnels. A total of 2,070 tons of ore sand are mined daily, producing 60,648 tons annually. Currently, the third layer is being mined, and the high mountain has been turned into a deep valley. After many years of excavation, the ore is nearly exhausted. The Dedao Bay section is divided into eight locations: Shishan Qianchang, Shishan Zhongchang, Shishan Qian Er Ceng, Shishan Hou Er Ceng, Shishan Hou San Ceng, Dashimen, Jiji Jianchang, and Shishilongdong, producing 396,000 tons of iron ore annually, totaling approximately 600,000 tons per year. A railway over fifty miles long has been laid from the mining area to Yuanjiahu. Yuanjiahu is the location of the mine factory, where iron ore enters the Yangtze River. The reporter arrived at the Yuanjiahu mine factory on the evening of the 5th. The factory area is large, and there are many workers. In the past, over ten thousand people worked there, and now there are no fewer than three to four thousand. Most of them are employed under a contracting system. Workers work eight hours a day, earning 12 cents per ton of ore mined. Generally, each person can earn 30 to 40 cents per day, and can also engage in agriculture. There is a compensation policy for deaths due to work-related accidents. Nearby farmers benefit greatly. However, due to debt relations, the factory is completely controlled by the Japanese. The laborers ultimately work hard, no different from working for others. On April 3, 1924, the factory borrowed 12 million Japanese yen from the Yawata Iron Works and the Yokohama Specie Bank in Japan, signing a contract to supply 15 million tons of ore sand and pig iron over ten years. On February 11, 1912, the Japanese government advanced 3 million yen and signed another contract. From then on, the ore sand was not allowed to be sold to other countries, and German engineers were replaced by Japanese engineers. On January 18, 1915, the Japanese government presented the Twenty-One Demands to Yuan Shikai, including Article 3, paragraphs 1 and 2, requesting that Hanyeping be jointly operated by China and Japan. The articles stated: "The two contracting parties mutually agree that when a suitable opportunity arises in the future, the Hanyeping Company will be operated jointly by the two countries, and unless with the consent of the Japanese government, the Chinese government shall not independently dispose of all rights and properties of the company." "The Chinese government especially allows all affiliated mines belonging to the Hanyeping Company to not be exploited by companies other than the company without the consent of the company, and agrees that if any borrowing is desired, whether directly or indirectly, that may affect the company, it must first be approved by the company." The Japanese government advanced from providing loans to implementing annexation, and subsequently, production declined sharply. Further loans were obtained from Japan, amounting to 30 million yen, bringing the total Japanese debt (including the entire Hanyeping) to 90 million yen. The Japanese then interfered with the factory's affairs as creditors, seizing sovereignty. Important positions such as chief engineer, engineer, chief accountant, and consultant were all filled by Japanese, and expenses exceeding 200 yuan were not valid without the signature of a Japanese. The situation was completely reversed, a complete disaster.

Xiangbishan Iron Mine 72

The Xiangbishan Iron Mine is located northwest of Daye County, in Jiangjiawan, not far from Huangshigang and Shihuiyao. A railway leads directly to Shenjiaying for export on the Yangtze River. The mine is divided into three areas, with the Xiangshan area being the main one, divided into four layers. The first and second layers are each over 70 feet high, the third layer is over 90 feet high, and the fourth layer is over 100 feet high. The second is the Laoshuwei area, divided into two layers, one over 50 feet high and the other over 40 feet high, connected to the Shishan of Hanyeping. The boundary was only recently established. The third is the Jianshan area, which has not yet been mined.

Xiangshan is connected to Shishan. Previously, there were no mining regulations, and those who purchased land privately had mining rights. It was initially owned by a private individual. Hanyeping Company took possession of it because its mining area was very large. The mountain owner was unwilling to be controlled by them, so the Hubei Official Currency Bureau took it over with 400,000 cash, making it provincial property. Planning began in 1918, and actual mining began in 1920. It was successively managed by the official mining supervision office, the official mining bureau, the agricultural department, and the construction department. Currently, the Construction Department has organized the "Xiangbishan Iron Mine Management Office," with three sections: mining, transportation, and research, and a newly added general affairs section.

The reporter visited the Laoshuwei mining area at 3:00 PM on the 6th, then transferred to Xiangbishan and arrived at the office. Because it was too late, I could only briefly view the mining equipment. There is a generator, boilers, lathes, planers, drilling machines, a foundry, and a carpentry shop, all of which should be available. The total capital is 6 million yuan, and the scale is of course much smaller than that of the Hanyeping factory. However, China has sovereign rights and has not been seized by others like Hanyeping, which is something to be proud of. The daily mining volume is 1,000 tons, or several hundred tons, because it is open-pit mining, the amount of mining cannot but depend on whether it is sunny or rainy. The sales market is the Liuhegou Yangtze Factory, which only sells 90,000 tons per year, and most of it still has to be sold to the Japanese. There are over 600 workers in the entire mine, divided into inside and outside workers. Inside workers earn more than 30 cents per day, and outside workers are dedicated to mining, earning 12 cents per ton. Most of them can earn 40 to 50 cents per day, and can also engage in agricultural work.

Fuhua Coal Mine 73

In the morning of the 7th, I went to visit the Fuhua Coal Mine Company. The mine is located in Huangshiwan, with lush trees and pleasant scenery, unlike the barren iron mountains. The person in charge of the company warmly welcomed me and led me into the mine. I changed into worker's clothes, put on long boots, carried a flashlight, and bravely entered with a walking stick. I fell down an 18-meter-deep shaft. The mine is divided into three entrances, with horizontal and vertical tunnels reaching over 20 li. The room and pillar method is used, which is the latest design by mining engineer Wang Jiliang and deputy mining engineer Song Jun. The mine is equipped with electric lights, pumps, and other equipment. Water sounds can be heard everywhere, which is very different from the dryness of the iron mine, and the danger is also greater than the iron mine. The coal miners all work naked, sweating profusely, covered in black coal, with only their eyes shining like ghosts. At first sight, it is quite frightening, but looking at myself, I am not much different, and I can't help but laugh. The workers dig coal with great difficulty. If they are lazy, the foreman's whip will immediately follow. I have seen several people being flogged, not daring to say a word. I walked in the mine for about three hours, and my waist and legs were tired. I left the mine at 6:00 PM, and a heavy mountain rain fell with loud thunder. This could not be heard in the mine at all.

The mine area is 452.50 hectares. It produces lignite and is entirely commercially operated with a capital of 560,000 yuan. Wuhan and the downstream areas are its sales markets. In recent years, due to the economic downturn in various markets and the impact of foreign coal dumping, sales have been extremely sluggish. There are currently 30,000 tons of coal in stock, piled up like mountains. At its peak, the mine had 1,300 to 1,400 workers, and at its lowest, 600 to 700 workers, divided into 20 groups. Management is also quite effective, but wages cannot be paid on time. In the future, workers must still be laid off and costs reduced to maintain operations. It is reported that the company is discussing that sales are now bad, and taxes are also high, including property tax, financial committee donation, union donation, chamber of commerce donation, public security donation, first district donation, second district donation, public welfare donation, and other miscellaneous donations, amounting to over 2,800 yuan per month, which is truly unbearable during the coal industry's decline.

Fuyuan Coal Mine 74

The Fuyuan Coal Mine is located in Tongzibao, Shihuiyao, with an area of 498.5378 hectares. It produces lignite, which is semi-anthracite, with an estimated reserve of 2 million tons. It was opened in the third year of Xuantong in the late Qing dynasty with a capital of 280,000 yuan, with Wuhan and the downstream of the Yangtze River, and the coastal ports of Fujian and Guangdong as sales markets, reaching 150,000 to 160,000 tons per year. Before 1931, profits were quite large. After the great flood, sales stagnated and prices fell, resulting in considerable losses and debts of about 200,000 yuan. The reporter visited the mine on the 8th, guided by Mr. Liu Liping to visit various places. The mine is divided into vertical shafts and horizontal tunnels. The vertical shaft is 200 meters deep, divided into two layers. There are two dark vertical shafts in the horizontal tunnel, each 100 meters deep. The caves are intricate, even more complex than Fuhua. There are about 1,200 workers, with the highest wages being about 50 cents per day and the lowest 30 cents. During prosperous times, there were still bonuses to be distributed. Each team elected a foreman to manage, and most of the short-term workers were nearby farmers. A worker representative office was also set up to facilitate contact with the employer. Currently, sales are sluggish, and inventory is piled up like a mountain. Wages have been in arrears for several months, the same as Fuhua. They are planning to merge with Fuhua, because the two mountains are connected, and mining will be more convenient after the merger, which can save expenses and jointly seek development. However, it is said that the opinions of the authorities on both sides are still inconsistent, and it is feared that it will be difficult to realize.

Lihua Coal Mine 75

The Lihua Coal Mine has a long history of using French methods of mining. It was renamed to its current name in 1928. The mine is located in Huangjingshan, eight li south of Dajiangbian in Shihuiyao. The coal is a type of anthracite white coal with strong ignition and heating power. The coal seam is only one, with an average thickness of two meters and a reserve of 15 million tons, with a daily output of 500 tons, which can be mined for 80 years. Its head office is located in Hankou, and the mining area has a mining office, with a branch office in Shihuiyao, from which the coal is exported. Because Shihuiyao is separated from the mining area by the Huangjingshan Mountains, and the mountain is rugged, it is impossible to lay a railway. A German Braesi Tow-line aerial cableway was specially built to facilitate coal transportation. The double cableway in the air is a great sight. The reporter was received by Deputy Cheng Xingjian at the branch office. Due to the strong wind and rain, I could not take the aerial cable car to visit the mine, which was quite a regret. According to Mr. Cheng, the mine's engineering equipment includes a well project, with east and west vertical shafts for coal output, each with a winder, 156 meters deep. Currently, it only reaches 125 meters. The horizontal tunnels are each 1,000 meters long. Coal mining is entirely manual. Hard rock roadways are excavated, with a part using pneumatic rock drills. There are 20 large and small pumps in the well, which can drain 1,000 tons of water per hour. The air outlet has an electric fan and an electric blower. The mining area currently has an area of 500 hectares. After being reorganized again in 1932, the capital was increased to 500,000, and 1 million was borrowed. All equipment was completed in one go. Coal sales are mainly in Wuhan, followed by Shanghai and Nanjing, followed by Zhenjiang, Fuzhou, Shantou, and Xiamen. Because the coal selection is better, sales are relatively smooth. There are currently 1,200 prospectors, divided into contractors and hourly workers. Contractors are paid either by the foot or by the ton. Large workers earn 3,800 wen, and small workers earn 2,000, with the foreman providing meals and paying monthly. Therefore, workers are quite hardworking. Compared with Fuhua and Fuyuan, it seems to have vitality.

The above mines used to employ a total of over 30,000 workers, which was enough to save the rural economy during times of panic. Now, each mine is declining daily, with the number of workers reduced to over 10,000, and their treatment is not as good as before. It is difficult to maintain the remaining situation. The prosperous times will not return. Thinking silently about the future, I can't help but feel terrified.

Travel Notes from Qinghai (Continued) 76

— Zhuang Juben

(3) The Mongolians of the Qunke Grassland

From the two Likjingles, we learned that there are eight Mongolian banners grazing in the Qunke Grassland. The density of banners is higher than anywhere else, such as Yongan and Qaidam, and it can be said to be a gathering place for the Mongolians of Qinghai. Now, all eight banners are listed below:

1. The Right Wing Leader of the Choros Tribe, Erlik Baylor, whose prince's name is Linqin Wangjile.

2. The Central Middle Banner of the Choros Tribe, Harge Beizi, whose prince's name is Zhashi Anmujile.

3. The Right Wing of the North Banner of the Khoshut Tribe, Zong Beizi, whose prince's name is Sonam Mu'andehai.

4. The Rear Banner of the Right Wing of the South Banner of the Khoshut Tribe, Tuo Mao Gong, whose Duke's name is Sonam Mu'pai Le.

5. The Rear Banner of the Left Wing of the South Banner of the Khoshut Tribe, Ake Gong, whose Duke's name is Labudan.

6. The Qunke Banner of the Left Wing of the South Banner of the Khoshut Tribe, Sack, whose Duke's name is Dan Zeng.

7. The Upper East Banner of the Khoshut Tribe, Bahaan Chorja Zasack, whose Duke's name is Le Duo Ri.

8. The Independent Banner, Chahan Qiejimen Khan (White Buddha) Zasack Grand Lama, whose name is Sui Ke Dai.

The Princes, Dukes, and Grand Lamas were all titles conferred by the Qing Dynasty. The subjects of each prince and duke are no more than a few hundred tents, or a few dozen tents, so their power is very small. The smallest banner, Bahaan Chorja Zasack, is said to have only two households. This prince is already nominal.

The Topography of the Qunke Grassland

On the 24th, the wind and clouds did not stop. In the morning, we watched the women milking cows at the door of the yurt. The cold wind and snow hit our faces, making us worry. Today, we planned to visit the pasture of Qunke Sack, but we heard that the prince had gone to Guanghui Temple in Datong a few days ago. Now we have to change our route to Chahannomen Khan to investigate the situation of the Independent Banner. At about ten o'clock, Erlik Beller sent Ula to see us off. Traveling west in the wind and snow, our hands and feet were frozen and sore.

After a journey of fifteen li, we crossed a river eight meters wide. The water had already frozen thick. The water source here is very narrow, drawing from its source. The river channel is slow and winding, stretching into the grassy mountains. A red rock mountain corner divides it into two tributaries, north and west.

The terrain on the grassland is open and gentle. The mountain slopes on both sides are gently sloping loess layers. Along the grassland, there is a depth that just passes the ankles. It reaches the upper reaches in the north, bordering Datong in the east, and facing Qinghai Lake on all sides. The area is also several hundred square miles, and the altitude is all above 3,000 meters above sea level. As the terrain goes up, the altitude gradually increases. Along the way, there are a few scattered yurts. Large herds of cattle and sheep are eating yellow grass, unafraid of the wind and snow. Now we climb that red rock mountain corner and cross the western tributary. The wind and snow slowly stopped.

Guided by the guide, we arrived at a village connected by adobe houses in the west. This is the home of the White Buddha. The owner of a tall adobe house welcomed us in. The stove with simmering mutton in the room was very warm.

The Tibetan Tribes of Mongolia

What is worth noting here is that their language is all Tibetan. At first, I thought that they were adjacent to the "Gangza" Tibetan tribe, so they could speak Tibetan. Later, I asked them, "Which ethnic group are you from?" And their reply, "We are Wu - Tibetan people."

Before coming, I already knew that Chahannomen Khan was an independent banner, without a prince but ruled by a Zasack Living Buddha. The Living Buddha is Tibetan and not Mongolian, so they are a special tribe. However, the results of investigations in all directions have now proven that not only is the ruling Zasack Lama Tibetan, but the ruled people are also Tibetan. There are a total of 6 tribes and 29 banners of Mongolians in Qinghai. Now Chahannomen Khan is a Mongolian banner that does not match its name. So the real Mongolians have only five tribes and twenty-eight banners. However, their special state of being Tibetan but Mongolian has aroused our historical interest.

They are a culturally backward nation without history, so it is difficult to know the evolution of their history. Later, in front of several elders, I obtained a small passage of legend:

Chahannomen Khan, the White Buddha, was sent from Tibet in ancient times to preach in Qinghai. Mongolians are very religious, so he often resides in Mongolian tribes. After Nian Gengyao pacified the west in the Qing Dynasty, he compiled Mongolians into banners and put him in the Mongolian banner, ruling Tibetans and becoming an independent banner, and was conferred the title of Zasack Grand Lama. Later, I obtained a more documented material from the Qinghai Southern Garrison Command in Xining:

During the Shunzhi period of the Qing Dynasty, the Tibetan Grand Lama Qi Yu Jiamu Cuo came to Qinghai to spread the teachings, and the Tibetan people obeyed and became the Seventh Hupilidong Khan. In the forty-fourth year of Kangxi (1705), the eighth Luo Bu Zang Jiamu Cuo entered the court and was granted the title of Chano Men, Khan Yongzheng awarded the title of Zasack in the third year. Chahannomen Khan is Mongolian, and the meaning of Khan in Han is "White Dharma King".

The Suffocation of the Lamb

This is the family of a steward of the White Buddha. The White Buddha is still very young, only ten years old this year, and is studying scriptures in a lama temple far away from here. He has 1,000 sheep, 300 cows, and 80 horses here, and his family property is not small. We wandered aimlessly in the village. Their houses are all three-dimensional bungalows. The building materials are only fir and loess, so the roofs and walls are mostly made of mud.

There are also farmland in the village. Their lives are half farming and half grazing. An average family cultivates five or six dou of land and raises dozens of sheep. The crops only produce highland barley, oats, and rapeseed, because the altitude is very high, already at 3,080 meters. The land freezes in July of the lunar calendar and thaws in March. There is often hail in summer. Last year, there was a severe hailstorm, so the crops were poor. In the past, this place was all pasture, and it was only reclaimed after 1919.

The climate is very cold. At 2:00 PM, there is a faint sunlight, and the thermometer still stays at minus five degrees. After eating tsampa and mutton, we also received a plate of mutton and a box of tsampa.

When we first arrived, the steward slaughtered a lamb to entertain us. A young lama took a fat sheep from the sheepfold and led it under the roof. He tied the four feet together and pushed it to the ground. Then he tightly wrapped the sheep's mouth with a woolen rope several times, preventing it from breathing. The lamb struggled on the ground, and the lama pressed it hard to prevent it from moving. After a quarter of an hour, the lamb's belly swelled and its eyeballs protruded. The lama found that it had suffocated, and then he started to skin it. The compassionate lama was also cruel for the sake of eating. The lamb's body was filled with purplish red hot blood, because the Tibetans like to eat blood-soaked meat (considering meat with blood as delicious), so the lamb is often subjected to such a cruel death.

There are more than a dozen adobe houses in the village, not many households, but the yurts nearby are all subjects of the Chahannomen Khan.

Social Life is Truly Free

We stayed in the village for two nights in total. The Tibetans nearby came to visit. The Tibetans here do not have any special clothing, only women. They also often wear Mongolian-style pointed hats, but there is no red thread tassel on them. Wealthy women hang many silver ornaments the size of bowls on their backs, usually twelve, four in a row, sewed on three wide belts, with a row of red tassels hanging below, and above are seven smaller silver ornaments or silver plates, directly connected to the ends of the braids in the middle of their heads. The silver ornaments are mostly engraved with beautiful patterns, with a red coral inlaid in the middle, very much like a pair of red knotted skullcaps. Their beautiful clothing weighs several pounds, which makes their heads feel heavy, so they use a leather cord to connect the decorations and tie them in front of their chests to reduce the burden on their heads. There are dozens of small braids around their heads, draped over their shoulders. Compared with ordinary Tibetan women, the Tibetan women here can all sing and dance. When we first arrived, we spent one yuan on wine in a merchant's yurt to invite them to sing. When they sing, they stand opposite each other, raising their sleeves and singing in a clear voice, but they sing more than they dance. The dancing movements are very simple, only raising their sleeves and turning around. It is also popular to sing and dance while toasting wine. When guests come, they sing a duet and offer a bowl of wine. Perhaps men and women are attracted to each other in the meeting, and they also sing and toast wine to each other to show their affection.

It is very common for girls to have a few days of free love among the Tibetans. According to the customs of marriage here, the new woman returns to her parents' home one day after entering the door, and only officially enters the door when she gives birth to a child. If the child is born late, and several years pass, then they will accommodate. Or, if the relationship between the couple is not good, then they will never come back like this. When the bride enters the door, two female attendants hold her armpits and walk through the gate of the man's house. The bride lowers her head and covers her face with her sleeves, showing her shy state.

Their social life is truly free. Today, a new guest wearing a fox fur hat came to the steward's house. At night, a beautiful Tibetan woman - a servant - slept with him in the kitchen. This was something that a sheep herder was very angry about and complained to the police about.

Songjiang: Sailboat Lost in Fog, Coal Oil Drifting 77

The Shanghai Guangkai Coal Oil Company, located at No. 14 Wubuyuan Road, previously loaded 200 barrels of San Gui coal oil and 1,300 pairs of new wicks onto the Zhang Qiaji Li Jiu sailboat to be shipped to Zhabei for sale. On the 3rd of this month, while sailing through the waters off Jinshanwei in this county, it suddenly encountered strong winds and waves, and dense fog covered the sky. The navigator lost direction and carelessly struck a reef. The sailboat sank, and all the coal oil drifted onto the sea, where it was secretly salvaged and profited from by local fishermen. The company's chairman, Xu Shiying, has telegraphed the county's Public Security Bureau to investigate. Director He has telegraphed the Ninth Precinct to investigate and seize [the stolen goods].

Kunshan: Expanding Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda 78

The Kunshan County's measures to expand anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda were decided upon at a meeting on the 9th. On the "6/3" Memorial Day, a public meeting will be held. In the afternoon, four teams will depart for propaganda. The rural areas will follow suit. Disguised speeches will be given by Kunshan Middle School students. A large number of Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug testaments will be printed and distributed, and many cautionary illustrations will be drawn and hung on various thoroughfares. Famous people will be invited to give speeches; County Magistrate Peng and others are being contacted. A speech contest against drug addiction will be held, organized and managed by the Education Bureau.

Determining Methods for Fundraising to Purchase an Airplane 79

This county has already decided on methods for raising funds to purchase an airplane for birthday celebrations. It is estimated that staff and members of the county party department will contribute more than 400 yuan; various government agencies and schools under the county government will collectively contribute approximately 6,000 yuan; and various businesses throughout the county will raise 4,000 yuan, totaling over 10,000 yuan. Active implementation will begin within days, with the aim of completion by the end of this month.

Suzhou: Fresh Meat Industry Decides to Suspend Slaughter for Three Days 80

The Wuxian Fresh Meat Industry Guild, due to the recent scarcity of pig supplies from Danyang, Jiangbei, and other places, despite discussions on the afternoon of the 9th to consider increasing fresh meat prices, due to the shortage of incoming goods, there will inevitably be no goods available for the market. Therefore, it was decided that starting today (the 10th), all meat shops in the city will uniformly suspend slaughter for three days, while sending personnel to Danyang and other places to purchase pigs in bulk to supply the market, and requesting the Slaughter Tax Collection Office to appropriately reduce the slaughter tax.

Student Lawsuit Against School Principal Awaits Judgment 81

Suzhou Anshi Middle School was established and funded by Cheng Wang Jichang, who resides in Xibaihua Lane. It has been five years since its establishment. However, the registration issue has not yet been resolved. More than ten graduates of another school, including Xu Guoyuan, concerned about the difficulty of transferring schools, specifically hired lawyers Zhou Yu and Zhang Yu to file a lawsuit with the Wuxian District Court, demanding that Cheng Wang Jichang compensate each student 2,000 yuan for losses. After repeated court hearings, the case has concluded, and the judgment is scheduled for 5:00 PM today (the 11th).

Changshu: Young Silkworms Not Developing Well 82

Wangzhuang, Yangjian, Langganqiao, and other places in the northwest of this area have traditionally been silkworm farming regions. This year, personnel were dispatched from the Silkworm Improvement Zone to provide guidance in the villages. Due to the uneven temperature this spring, the spring silkworms have been affected. The current silkworm rearing method involves joint rearing of young silkworms by the guidance center. However, hatching and the arrival of ant-like larvae are uneven. The early batches have already reached the third molt, while the late batches have not yet turned into ant-like larvae. The future harvest will inevitably be affected, and the general villagers are extremely anxious.

Corpse of Murdered Man Discovered by Lakeside 83

Yesterday afternoon (the 9th), the corpse of a murdered man was discovered by Kuncheng Lake in Youdun Village, outside Xiaodongmen. He had eleven knife wounds on his body, and half of his head and neck had been severed, a truly tragic sight. The village reported to the county for inspection. The corpse was particularly unusual. The first discoverer was a fisherman. The corpse was wrapped in a cotton quilt, then further wrapped in a straw mat and bound with ropes. The corpse's feet were particularly long, and they were curled up and tightly bound inside. Examination revealed five knife wounds on the face, half of the neck severed, and six knife wounds on the chest. It was confirmed that he had been murdered before being thrown into the river to eliminate traces. The county government has already ordered the village guards to collect and bury [the body] and is conducting a careful investigation.

Wuxi: Bandits Rob at Night 84

In Chen Sifang, Meicun Town, Second District of this county, a widow, Madam Chen, is over forty years old. Her husband, Chen Fengwei, has passed away, leaving behind a beloved son of fourteen years. The family is of modest means, which attracted the covetousness of bandits. Last night (the 9th) at around 10 PM, four bandits suddenly arrived, each wielding iron bars and flashlights, and broke into the house. At that time, Madam Chen and her son were awakened from their sleep and got out of bed to prepare to hide. Unexpectedly, they were grabbed by the bandits and forbidden to make a sound. The bandits ransacked the boxes and chests, stealing 340 yuan in legal tender and one merchant's scale. After obtaining the loot, the bandits fled to the north.

Huishan Begins Land Survey of Mountainous Areas 85

Since the Land Administration Bureau of this county began handling land registration in various districts, its work has become even more intensive. Director Hu has specially dispatched Registration Director Yan Baozi and Supervisor Bi Haoru to inspect various registration sub-offices starting yesterday, for approximately one week, after which they will return to the bureau. The land survey of Huishan began on the 1st of this month. However, a small number of grave tenants are taking the opportunity to extort money by creating false claims when the owners are inserting boundary markers. Director Hu has reported this to the county magistrate, who has jointly issued a public notice. In the future, if the above-mentioned situation is discovered, once reported by the owner, and confirmed to be true, it will be investigated and dealt with, without leniency.

Changzhou: Two More Opium Addicts Die in Detention 86

The Anti-Smoking Association of Wujin County recently conducted a general roundup of opium addicts. The various public security branch bureaus and district and town offices apprehended many opium addicts, some of whom were sent to rehabilitation centers for treatment, while others were detained in opium addict outposts. After entering the facilities, although they were given medicinal solutions, they still felt extremely pained. There have been multiple deaths due to illness. The county government has ordered prison officials and rehabilitation centers to properly treat sick inmates and administer medicinal solutions on time. However, there are so many sick inmates that two more, Chen Bingkun and Qian Zhengfa, died on the 9th. Prison official Li Yurui reported this to the Procuratorate of the District Court, which dispatched personnel for examination, and preparations were made for burial.

Bengbu: Improving Tea Production in Western Anhui 87

Western Anhui is known for its tea production, particularly the yellow tea from Huoshan, which is highly regarded. Annual tea revenue amounts to no less than eight or nine hundred thousand yuan. The new tea is already on the market, and it is said that prices are still good at the beginning of the season. The county's Tea Industry Guild believes that most tea farmers still cling to old habits in tea harvesting and production, adhering to outdated methods and failing to make improvements. They often over-manipulate the original tea quality, reduce drying and roasting, and mix in old, coarse leaves to deceive tea merchants and profit from it. As a result, the reputation of tea from this region in the Shandong and Hebei markets has plummeted in recent years, causing tea merchants to be at a loss. If this continues, sales will be blocked, and no one will inquire, which will have a profound and significant impact on the national economy and people's livelihood. In order to urgently seek a remedy, they have drafted measures to improve tea production and submitted them to the county government, requesting the elimination of old methods of harvesting and production commonly used by tea farmers, such as restricting tender leaf picking, prohibiting mixing of grades, and ensuring proper roasting. Detailed instructions have been given. It has been learned that the Huoshan County Government has expanded the presentation and strictly ordered various districts to instruct chiefs and heads of the Baojia system to earnestly implement these measures, urging all tea farmers and tea shops to comply with the improvements, so as to facilitate sales and save the rural areas.

Local News

Shanghai Fish Market Grand Opening This Morning: Decorations Mimic Fish Shapes, Invitations Extended to All Sectors for Ceremony; Business Regulations Announced Yesterday, Opening Tomorrow Morning; Market Petitions Navy for Warship Escort for Fishing; Board Meeting Last Night Approves List of Brokers 88

The Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industries, since its preparation, has completed all arrangements and is scheduled to hold a grand opening ceremony at 10:00 AM today. The details are as follows: The market has sent invitations to all sectors to attend the ceremony. The auction venue outside the office has been selected as the opening ceremony site. A platform will be erected at the main entrance, and the flags of the party and the nation, as well as the portrait of the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen, will be hung. The market will be fully decorated with national flags and exquisitely crafted red and green fish lanterns, unique and unseen elsewhere. A banner with the words "Grand Opening Ceremony of the Shanghai Fish Market" will be hung outside. A pine and cypress archway will be erected at the entrance, with a registration area set up underneath. Daily necessities shops and tea stalls will be set up around the periphery to meet the needs of the guests. A portion of the market's office will be temporarily converted into a lounge for receptions. The market's architecture is purely fish-shaped. With these decorations, it is very novel. It is expected that many people will come this morning to admire the scenery of this new-style island nation architecture.

Designated Staff: The opening ceremony staff, designated from the market's staff, are as follows: Chairman: Du Yuesheng; Master of Ceremonies: Sun Yizhuo; Recorders: Shao Piaoping, Yang Zongkai; Reception: In addition to various secretaries and section chiefs, Chairman Gu is naturally a receptionist, and the following members are also designated: City Ferry Terminal: Ling Zhibin, Zhou Buliang, Liu Lifu, Lin Changzhi; Dinghai Bridge Terminal: Dai Baoda, Ren Xieqing; Market Entrance: Zhu Youren, Zheng Xizuo; Meeting Venue: Qu Junyuan, Shao Piaoping, Yuan Hegao, Sheng Yujun, Ling Anlan; Female Guest Reception: Zhu Molan, Zhu Peizheng; Secretaries: Qian Shaoxun, Zhang Renbang, Qian Shutang, Wu Chucai, Zhang Puren, Shao Jiasen; Transportation: Ling Zhibin, Zhou Buliang, Liu Lifu, Lin Changzhi, Dai Baoda, Ren Xieqing; Tour Guides: Yao Huanzhou, Zhang Zhuzun, Shi Yunjie, Zhang Yousheng.

Routes to the Market: The market is located on Dinghai Island in the Huangpu River, far from the center of Shanghai. The market's office originally planned to provide car service at the City Ferry Terminal on the Bund of Beijing Road, but now, since the City Ferry Terminal has arranged Ferry No. 6 to transport guests, the market will no longer provide car service. Ferry No. 6 will depart from the Bund terminal of Beijing Road at 5:20 AM today and go directly to the Dinghai Island Fish Market. All guests can wait at the terminal before 9:20 AM. The Fish Market will send staff to the terminal to take care of things after 8:30 AM.

Opening Tomorrow Morning: After the Fish Market opens this morning, it will begin operations at 3:00 AM tonight (i.e., 3:00 AM tomorrow morning). Currently, various fish businesses are enthusiastically participating in the market as brokers or wholesalers. Although some fish businesses had previously expressed non-cooperation and intended to operate in Xiaodongmen, the City Chamber of Commerce is advising them, so there should be no problems. As for the brokers, the market will give priority to fish businesses joining, and the market has notified the Fish Industry Association to inform all fish businesses that it will not monopolize.

Yesterday's Meeting: At 3:00 PM yesterday, the market's board of directors held a meeting at the China Exchange Bank to review the brokers. Attendees included Chairman Du Yuesheng, Resident Supervisor Qian Xinzhi, Executive Directors Fang Jiaobo, Tang Chengzong, Kui Yanfang, General Manager Wang Xiaolai, Deputy General Managers Zhu Kaiguan, Sun Guchen, and many others. The meeting adjourned late in the evening. According to a reporter from Dagong News Agency, the quota of fish market brokers has been determined to be forty. The twenty-eight firms are Qu Changshun, Tongrenchang, Yurun, Hengtai, Yongtai, Shen Baoji, Fuji, Yuanli, Hongji, Fenghao, Shunda, Huifeng, Dahe, Binghui, Yuanmao, Yuanchang, Jiuji, Daji, Liji, Yuanchang, Haifeng, Shunyuan, Fengshun, Qinyi, Yongyuan, Yongxing, Yuanyuan, and Wenji. The above brokers have been announced by the market. The remaining twelve quotas are reserved for fish businesses that are members of the Seafood Trade Association.

Naval Escort for Fishing: Since its establishment, the Shanghai Fish Market has been very concerned about the interests of fishermen. In order to protect the safety of fishermen and increase fish production, it submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry to forward to the Navy Department yesterday, requesting the dispatch of warships to escort fishing. The original text is as follows: "Regarding the matter of petitioning, the fishing administration scope of the market is of utmost importance to the protection of fishing. Now that the Fishing Protection Office has been abolished, it is insufficient to maintain protection without borrowing the power of the fleet. It is most appropriate for the gunboats of the Ning-class fleet of the First Fleet of the Navy Department to protect fishing. It is requested that your ministry consult the Navy Department and order the Coast Guard Command of the First Fleet to designate the gunboats for the specific purpose of protecting fishing. Respectfully submitted for your review and approval. Respectfully submitted to Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry, General Manager Wang Xiaolai, Deputy General Managers Zhu Kaiguan, Sun Guchen."

Announcement of Regulations: The market's board of directors announced the revised business regulations yesterday as follows: Business Regulations of Shanghai Fish Market Co., Ltd. Chapter I: General Provisions. Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 46 of the Articles of Association of Shanghai Fish Market Co., Ltd. Article 2: The types of fish traded in the fish market are stipulated as follows: Marine fish; Freshwater fish; Salted and dried fish; Other aquatic products. The first transaction of the above fish entering Shanghai must be conducted in the fish market. Article 3: The daily opening and closing hours of the market shall be determined and announced by the fish market. Article 4: The holidays of the fish market are stipulated as follows: National Day; New Year's Day; Days generally closed for business in Shanghai commercial custom. The fish market may open on holidays if it deems necessary. Chapter II: Wholesalers. Article 5: Fish market wholesalers are limited to citizens of the Republic of China. The fish market shall appoint one person each from the marine fish industry and the river fish industry. When necessary, the fish market may appoint one additional person. Article 6: Wholesalers may appoint agents, but only limited to the original marine fish and river fish industries. Article 7: The wholesaler's agent shall fill out a letter of application and resume, which shall be submitted by the wholesaler to the fish market for registration. After approval, a badge shall be issued. The same shall apply to replacements. Article 8: Wholesalers shall be exclusively engaged in the business of selling fish on behalf of cargo owners. Marine fish shall be handled by the marine fish industry, and river fish shall be handled by the river fish industry. Other aquatic products shall be temporarily designated by the fish market from time to time. Article 9: Wholesalers shall abide by all rules and regulations of the fish market. If there is any violation, the fish market may impose sanctions. The sanction methods shall be determined separately. Article 10: Wholesalers of marine fish may charge cargo owners a service fee of 2% of the cargo price, but the fee shall be halved if the cargo owner has not borrowed cargo capital. Wholesalers of river fish may charge cargo owners a service fee of 30 cents per dan. Of the service fees collected for marine fish and river fish, one-quarter shall be used as the fish market's handling fee. Chapter III: Brokers. Article 11: Fish market brokers are limited to citizens of the Republic of China. The quota is temporarily set at 40 people. If necessary, the number may be increased or decreased at any time upon resolution of the board of directors. Article 12: Those who have any of the following circumstances shall not be fish market brokers: Those without capacity for civil conduct; Those who have been declared bankrupt; Those who have been deprived of public rights and have not yet been restored; Those who have been sentenced to imprisonment of one year or more and have not completed the execution or have been pardoned for less than five years; Those who have been expelled from the fish market for less than three years. Article 13: Anyone who intends to be a fish market broker shall fill out a letter of application and resume, along with proof of experience in the fish industry, and provide a security deposit of 5,000 yuan and a letter of guarantee from two reputable stores. The application shall be submitted to the fish market for review and approval, and then submitted to the Ministry of Industry for the issuance of a business license. However, the fish market shall give priority to approving those who are originally members of the Fish Industry Association or shareholders with 50 or more shares in the market and apply to be brokers in accordance with the regulations. If a broker is permitted by the board of directors, he may use other guarantee methods to replace cash, but the payment for the transaction shall be cleared on the same day. Article 14: Brokers shall be responsible to the fish market for all liabilities arising from their transactions. Article 15: Brokers shall not use improper methods to participate in auctions, and shall not use secret language or codes during auctions. Article 16: Brokers may appoint agents to represent their business. Article 17: When a broker appoints an agent, he shall submit the agent's resume to the fish market for review and approval before it becomes effective. When an agent is dismissed, the broker shall report the reasons for the dismissal to the fish market for record. Article 18: Brokers shall set up a business office within the area designated by the fish market. Article 19: The fish market shall stipulate the format of the account books and documents used by brokers in transactions, and may request them for inspection at any time. If there is any inquiry, it shall be answered immediately. Article 20: Brokers and their agents shall be issued badges by the fish market. Those without badges shall not be allowed to enter the market to participate in auctions. If they are lost or damaged, they shall request a replacement. The badges issued to brokers or agents shall not be lent or given to others. Article 21: Brokers shall strictly abide by the rules and regulations of the fish market and shall not violate them. Article 22: When a broker ceases business, he shall submit a letter stating the reasons for the cessation of business and return the business license and admission badge to the fish market. However, if there are unfinished transactions or payments that have not been cleared, he shall not cease business. Article 23: When a broker is expelled, if there are unfinished transactions, the broker shall settle them himself. If he cannot settle them, the fish market shall designate another broker to settle them on his behalf. Any losses shall be borne by the broker. Article 24: If a broker violates any of the following circumstances, the fish market may temporarily suspend his transactions or expel him: Those who fail to deliver the goods or money after being pursued in accordance with the provisions of Article 45, Paragraph 1; Those who delay payment for goods; Those whose behavior obstructs the business of the fish market and there is solid evidence; Those who have not purchased fish from the fish market for more than ten days; Those whose total amount of fish purchased each month is less than 5,000 yuan; Those who violate the rules and regulations of the fish market. Chapter IV: Brokers' Association. Article 25: Brokers shall organize a brokers' association to promote their common business interests and correct their malpractices. Article 26: The regulations and resolutions of the brokers' association shall be effective only after being approved by the fish market. If the fish market deems it inappropriate, it may order it to be corrected in whole or in part. Chapter V: Transaction Methods. Article 27: The cargo owner shall issue a letter of entrustment to the fish market for the fish entrusted for transaction by himself or his agent. The letter of entrustment shall specify the quantity and minimum selling price of each type of fish. If the selling price is not specified, the fish market may sell it at an appropriate price on its behalf. Article 28: Not limited to those permitted by the fish market. The fish entrusted in accordance with the preceding paragraph shall still pay the corresponding handling fee, the amount of which shall be determined separately. Article 30: The fish entrusted for transaction, which has been delivered to the fish market for counting and has a receipt, shall be kept in custody by the fish market. If there is any loss, it shall be compensated by the fish market, but the loss due to the reduction in weight and consumption, and due to climate and force majeure, shall not be limited. Fish that has not been landed and handed over to the fish market may be used as a sample to be entrusted to the fish market for transaction, but the cargo owner shall be responsible for keeping it in custody. Article 31: Fish entrusted for transaction shall be sold by the fish market by means of auction, but in any of the following circumstances, the fish market may sell it by other means: 1. When it is considered that it is not practically suitable for sale by means of auction; 2. When the quantity of fish is too large, or the arrival is too late, and it is considered that the auction is difficult; 3. When the use of auction methods is likely to depress the cargo price; 4. When it is considered necessary to use other trading methods. Article 32: The language used in the implementation of the auction shall be mainly Mandarin, but local common languages may be used as appropriate. Article 33: The fish market shall auction fish in the order of the cargo owner's entrustment. Article 34: If any of the following circumstances exist, the fish market may refuse to negotiate a transaction: 1. Those that have deteriorated or are harmful to hygiene; 2. Those that are prohibited by law to be captured or sold. Article 35: Only fish market wholesalers, brokers and their agents may participate in the auction. Article 36: If a broker purchases fish within the Shanghai area without passing through the fish market, the fish market shall, in addition to estimating its fish price and collecting the handling fee in accordance with the regulations, also have the right to expel it. Article 37: After the fish transaction is completed, the fish market shall immediately register it in the book. Article 38: If the fish market considers the auction price to be inappropriate, it may stop the auction at any time. Article 39: If the fish entrusted for transaction does not reach the specified price, the provisions of the preceding article shall be followed. Article 40: After the transaction is completed and registered in the book, the fish market shall immediately send a statement of account to the wholesaler and the broker. Neither party shall raise any objection to the determined transaction. Article 41: After the transaction is completed, the broker shall immediately receive the purchased fish and immediately move it away from the auction site. Article 42: Once the fish has been received, the broker shall be responsible for its custody. If there is any loss, it shall not be related to the fish market. For fish that has not been landed and handed over to the fish market, but is sold only as a sample, the broker shall also receive it immediately after the transaction is completed and immediately move it away from the fish storage place without delay. If there is any dispute regarding the acceptance of this fish, it shall be resolved by the fish market. Both parties shall comply and shall not object. Article 43: If the broker delays receiving and moving away the purchased fish without justified reason, all losses shall be borne by the broker. Article 44: The fish market shall immediately pay the proceeds from the sale of the fish to the wholesaler, who shall then transfer it to the cargo owner, after deducting the handling fee and other fees that should be paid. Article 45: The money that the broker should pay to the fish market shall be cleared every five days, but in any of the following circumstances, the fish market may pursue it at any time: 1. The amount of unpaid goods always exceeds the stipulated maximum limit, which shall be determined and announced by the fish market at its discretion; 2. When a broker is expelled or suspended from participating in auctions. Article 46: If the broker cannot pay the outstanding amount for the goods, the fish market may deduct it from the security deposit. If there is any deficiency, it shall be recovered from the guarantor. Article 47: For transactions made by a broker entrusted by a customer, the fish market only recognizes the broker as the subject of the transaction. All matters relating to the transaction of the person who entrusted it may be handled directly with the broker he entrusted, and shall not be related to the fish market. Article 48: A broker who is entrusted by a customer to purchase goods may charge a commission of 1.5% of the cargo price. Chapter VI: Arbitration. Article 49: When a dispute arises between a broker and a client due to a entrustment relationship and a request is made to the fish market for arbitration, the fish market shall temporarily appoint three or more arbitrators from among the staff and the brokers' association staff to organize an arbitration committee to deliberate and judge. If an arbitrator is involved in an event involving his own or his relatives' interests, he shall apply for recusal. Chapter VII: Commission. Article 50: The fish market charges a commission of 7% of the cargo price for selling goods entrusted for transaction. Article 51: The fish market shall distribute the commission collected in the following amounts to the wholesaler and the broker: Wholesaler: 1.25%; Broker: 1.75%. Article 52: In addition to the various fees collected as stipulated in these regulations, wholesalers and brokers shall not collect other fees. All bad customs shall be abolished. Violators shall be punished in accordance with the regulations and severely punished by the Ministry of Industry. Article 53: If the fish market deems it necessary, it may change the amount stipulated in the preceding two articles at any time, and report it to the Ministry of Industry for record. Chapter VIII: Supplementary Provisions. Article 54: For all matters not stipulated in these rules, the fish market may temporarily announce their implementation. Article 55: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Preparation Process: Mr. Yao Huanzhou, the current chief technician of the market and former member of the preparatory committee, yesterday published the preparation process as follows: "During the term of Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry, there was a plan to develop the fishing industry, open fishing ports, and build fish markets. Minister Chen continued to follow Minister Kong's original intention and regarded the development of the fishing industry and the establishment of fish markets as one of the urgent industries to be improved. In October of the 23rd year, Hou Zhaohai, Zhang Zhuzun, and others were sent to Japan to investigate the organization of fish markets, so as to prepare for the establishment of a fish distribution agency. Shanghai is an international and national important market, with four major cities standing on three sides. Coastal ships and land transportation are concentrated here. The products of the whole country are discharged in this area. Therefore, it is proposed to establish a fish market in Shanghai as a national pioneer. By January of the 23rd year, this plan and estimate were submitted to the Executive Yuan and approved by the Central Political Conference. It was decided to be jointly operated by the government and merchants. In February, Yu Kaizhan, Xu Tinghu, Hou Zhaohai, Yao Huanzhou, Feng Limin, and other seven people were appointed as members of the preparatory committee to establish the Shanghai Fish Market Preparatory Committee on Sichuan Road. The preparatory committee appointed Zhang Zhuzun, Wang Chong, Wang Defa, Shen Zutong, and others as design committee members to actively proceed in accordance with the plan approved by the Central Political Conference. It took 22 months. The plenary meeting of all committee members was held for six times, and the Standing Committee for 116 times. The first estimated budget of the market, which was submitted to and approved by the Central Political Conference, was a total of 1,671,000 yuan. Based on the principle of joint government-merchant operation, since the recruitment of commercial shares was difficult and because the site of the Pujiang Bureau was leased, the original land purchase fee of 500,000 yuan was deleted. The Ministry of Industry submitted a request to the Central Political Conference to reduce it to 1 million yuan, of which 500,000 yuan was paid by the national treasury, and the remaining 500,000 yuan was invested by merchants. By March of this year, Minister Wu and Mr. Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Kui Yanfang, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Kaiguan, and Sun Guchen decided after repeated discussions that the continued fixed expenses of 1 million yuan were really insufficient. After the government and merchants reviewed the results, Minister Wu submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to increase the previously determined budget from 1 million yuan to 1.2 million yuan, with the principle that the government and merchants would each invest half. Commercial shares were recruited for 300,000 yuan first, and the Ministry of Industry would subsidize 600,000 yuan. The amount insufficient for commercial shares would be subsidized by the Ministry of Industry. As for the site, the newly filled land of the Pujiang Bureau, Dinghai Island, the current site of the market, was leased. It was chosen for its wide river surface and suitable water depth. Ships with a draft of about 20 feet can dock at will, regardless of high or low tide. After a long period of consultation and personnel mediation, the decision was finally made. However, the rent is high, with a value of more than 700 yuan per mu per year, totaling 47 mu and 6 fen, and an annual rent of more than 30,000 yuan must be paid. By April of this year, the founding meeting was established, and it can be opened today."

Detailed Engineering Record: The site of the Shanghai Fish Market is located on the newly filled滩地of Dinghai Island, Yangshupu, Pujiang Bureau, covering a total area of 238.3872公亩. The north-south length along the Pujiang River is 182.88 meters (600 feet), the east-west length on the north side is 130.7 meters (492 feet), the east-west length on the south side is 152.4 meters (500 feet), and the north-south length on the west side is 179.22 feet (588 feet). The main buildings include: (A) Fish Market Office Building: Ground floor, Second floor, Third floor, Fourth floor, Fifth floor, Sixth floor, Seventh floor. The height of each floor: Ground floor is 3.962 meters (13 feet), the second and third floors are 3.553 meters (11 feet), the fourth, fifth and sixth floors are 2.74 meters (9 feet), and the seventh floor is 2.591 meters (6 feet). (B) Auction Site: Area of 1517.22 square meters (16332 square feet), north-south length of 64.49 meters (211.7 feet), east-west length of 21.67 meters (71.2 feet), east of the fishing boat dock, north of the Fish Market Office Building, west of the broker's office, building height of 6.48 meters (21.1 feet). (C) Temporary Warehouse Auction Site: Four temporary warehouses are built along the dock on the east-west side, each 12.80 meters (42 feet) long, 8.077 meters (25.1 feet) wide, and 4.318 meters (14.2) high. (D) Cold Storage Room: Area of 1788.88 square meters (19256 square feet), east-west length of 67.11 meters (220.2), north-south length of 25.4 meters (83.4), with five large cold storage rooms, two manager's rooms, one ice-making room, two freezing rooms, two machine rooms, and several processing rooms. (E) Dock: Shore length of 182.88 meters (600), existing floating dock of 177.69 meters (53). (G) Broker's Office: Area of 1429.64 square meters (8495.19 square feet), two floors in total. The upper floor will be built in the northern section first, and can be added at any time as needed. The ground floor is the broker's office, with 27 offices, each with an area of 1 square国×40.5 ( ). There is also a toilet. The second floor is the business office of each fishing vessel company, with 25 offices, two toilets, one storage room, and a cold storage room, including a freezing room, a cold storage room, an ice-making room, a machine room, pipe installation, transformer room equipment, and other machinery.

Yu Shunqing Reports on the Discovery of Oil Wells: Abundant Oil in the Wells, Locals Use it for Salt Production; Chemical Tests Show It Also Contains Potassium, Sodium, and Iodine 91

Yu Shunqing, a standing committee member of the National Coal Production and Sales Federation in this city, believes that Sichuan province has abundant oil resources, readily available everywhere. It is regrettable that Chinese people do not know how to exploit them, resulting in the waste of resources. In order to promote domestic oil and prevent financial leakage, he has specially united with both political and business circles to organize the Puli Oil Company and actively carry out operations. In addition to spending days running around seeking support from all sides, Yu also sent letters yesterday reporting on the discovery of oil wells in Sichuan province. Excerpts from his original text are as follows: "Since our country wants to seek national prosperity and strength, and improve social welfare, we must devote ourselves to production. Moreover, looking at the success of Russia's Five-Year Plan, its booming production has amazed countries all over the world. Modern

Scientific progress requires the use of machinery for any production undertaking. Therefore, the uses of iron and coal are extensive and significant. Furthermore, since the invention of airplanes and the popularity of automobiles, factories and ships also compete to use engines. As a result, the need for petroleum surpasses that of coal. Although our country has wide coal-producing areas, most rely on native methods of mining, resulting in high prices and low production, which provides an opportunity for foreign coal to enter. Shunqing, though not talented, once organized the Puli Coal Company, dedicated to circulating domestic coal. He also initiated the National Coal Production and Sales Federation with prominent figures in Shanghai, appealing loudly, hoping to work with gentlemen in the country to promote it. Remembering that the supply of coal and oil completely depends on imported goods, he was always concerned and puzzled. Recently, he heard that in the Zigong area of Sichuan, in addition to extracting salt water from salt wells, a kind of oily substance is produced. After analysis and chemical use,

It is petroleum. Hearing this, he was overjoyed and immediately prepared travel expenses to Sichuan. Regardless of the hardships, he happily packed his bags and set off, personally going to Zigong for on-the-spot investigation. Thanks to the hospitality of local people, they told me everything and gave me samples of analyzed well oil and various brines to take back to Shanghai for formal chemical testing. Now, I present my findings to all of you, hoping for your guidance. The only well I saw dug was a hundred zhang deep, and the brine was inexhaustible. Each unit could produce twenty catties of salt. When the well water is first drawn, it is all oily, light in quality, and combustible. The locals use it for lighting lamps and call it well oil. After the oil is exhausted, it becomes brine, clear in color, turning yellow after three hours. The locals call it yellow water. There is also gas discovered in the well, which the locals use

Connect pipes to ignite the fire, like the Shanghai gas lamps, to boil brine for salt. The locals call it well water. If you dig to two hundred zhang, you must pass through hard rock layers. Each dan of brine can produce more than forty catties of salt, and the color is either black or grayish-white. The locals call it black water. In the Dawenbao area, there is another type of rock formation. The extraction method is to first pour clear water into the well and then extract it. The quality is very salty, and each dan can produce eighty catties of salt. The locals call it salt rock water. When boiling, they all use gas to connect pipes for burning. The situation is similar in Gongjing, fifteen li away from Zigong, but salt rock has not yet been discovered. The locals rely on manual labor to dig wells. If they dig to three hundred and fifty zhang or three hundred and twenty zhang, red rock is found below. The soil is loose, similar to the surface soil. Geologists call it the boundary between the Triassic and Permian periods. An American gentleman once investigated the area and said that if wells are dug to four hundred zhang or below, kerosene can be extracted. Its

Abundant oil reserves, can be extracted without end. Someone once proposed a plan to initiate exploitation, but it failed to raise funds, and the proposal was shelved. Upon inquiry, the salt water was analyzed by Mr. Tan Shoutian, Director of the Central Geological Survey, and technician Jin Kaiying eighteen years ago. In addition to potassium and sodium, iodine was found. If a method can be devised to extract these two substances, it would also be a great source of profit. Shunqing is old and unable to do anything. I dare to express my sincerity, hoping that gentlemen and young people in the country will jointly fulfill this great wish, exploit this inexhaustible source of profit, wash away the shame of relying entirely on imported goods, and elevate our country to prosperity and strength. This is what I pray for fervently. The results of the chemical testing by the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau's Industrial Chemistry Testing Institute, Testing Form No. 930, are recorded on the left."

Zhejiang Provincial Government Borrows 840,000 from the China and Communications Banks 93

The Hangzhou Branch Sends a Telegram to the Head Office Seeking Instructions, Hoping to Succeed; Pledging New Public Bonds Worth 1.4 Million at a 60% Discount

The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in order to reorganize Zhejiang's finances and unify local public bonds, specially obtained approval from the central government to issue 60 million yuan of the 25th Year Zhejiang Provincial Reorganization Public Bonds. In addition to the 55 million yuan needed to reorganize old debts, there is still a surplus of 5 million yuan. Germany Tightens Trade Controls, Chinese Goods Linger in German Ports, Exporters Request Assistance from the International Trade Bureau to Cope with the Planned Sino-German Trade Payment Method 94

The Shenshi News Agency reports that China's exports to Germany mainly include eggs and egg products, peanuts, casings, bristles, lace, tablecloths, etc. However, since Germany implemented exchange controls, the impact on China's export trade with Germany has been profound. Because Germany's trade controls are very strict, the German government does not allow the proceeds from goods exported from China to Germany to be repatriated, but limits it to local consumption. With the permission of the German government, real estate can be purchased in Germany. If German goods are to be purchased back, three times the original value of the goods must be paid. Through the above three measures, Germany strictly restricts the outflow of cash, causing China's exports to Germany to be unable to recover payment for goods, which has become a thorny issue for Chinese exporters to Germany, making it impossible to develop. Therefore, Shanghai Kaiji Trading Company and other exporters to Germany have requested the International Trade Bureau to find ways to provide relief. The bureau is doing its best to provide assistance in order to maintain the past prosperity of trade with Germany. It is now planned to first unite importers and exporters who have trade relations with Germany and implement local purchasing through transfer or substitution methods as a temporary remedy. They will also contact each other and notify export trading firms dealing with Germany that they can consult with the bureau on this issue in the future.

Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement: Proposals from the Standing Committee Meeting of the Lawyers Association 95

The Standing Committee of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Republic of China Lawyers Association convened a meeting yesterday (Sunday) at 10:00 AM at the Shanghai Lawyers Association. Committee members Liu Zuwang, Chen Dexin, Chen Zhigao, Kuai Jinde, Wang Weizhen, etc. attended. Liu Zuwang was elected as chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the minutes. The meeting proceeded as planned. The proposals are recorded below: 1. Request the Legislative Yuan to enact a law on compensation for wrongful imprisonment. Resolved: Continue to request the enactment, send committee member Shen Junru to Nanjing to request the Legislative Yuan, and notify local lawyers associations of the draft proposal to advocate it unanimously. 2. Request the Judicial Yuan to submit the draft law on compensation for wrongful imprisonment passed by the National Judicial Conference to the Legislative Yuan for enactment. Resolved: Approved. 3. Request the Secretary-General of the Lawyers Association to transfer all documents related to the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Committee to the Shanghai Lawyers Association so that the Standing Committee can handle them nearby to improve efficiency. Resolved: Approved. 4. Regarding the reports from local lawyers associations on the progress of the wrongful imprisonment movement, the association should collect materials and hand them over to the Standing Committee for editing and compilation. Resolved: Approved. The deadline for publication is the end of May. 5. How to promote the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Day on June 5? Resolved: Local lawyers associations will continue to hold events with the following methods: (A) In addition to those who already have a Wrongful Imprisonment Committee, each association should organize and establish a Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Committee before the end of May. (B) Set June 5 to 11 as Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week. Each association should choose one day within this week to hold activities and report the movement plan and progress to the association for compilation in a special issue next year. (C) Unite local legal entities to jointly promote the movement in accordance with the publicity guidelines to increase effectiveness. (D) In addition to issuing declarations, each local association should draft its own declaration. (E) Before Wrongful Imprisonment Movement Week, local party, government, legal, and educational circles, as well as other sectors, should be responsible for hospitality, and each association should consider the methods themselves. 6. The association's legal journal should be asked to publish a special issue. Resolved: Approved. 7. The 9th Plenary Session of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee will be convened on May 31. Resolved: Approved. The location will be notified later. The meeting adjourned.

The Shiye News Agency reports that the Shanghai Money Industry Association held the 15th Executive Committee meeting of the 3rd session at the Ningbo Road Association yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. It was resolved to send separate letters to the five closed money firms, including Futai, to investigate the debts and report to the Supervisory Committee, and to hold a summer managerial meeting on June 16th. Details are as follows:

Attending Committee Members. Those who attended yesterday included Liu Wuqiao, Shao Yanshan, Wang Jiemei, Shen Jingliang, Ye Xiuchun, Xi Jiming, Wu Zilin, Zhang Wenbo, Zhang Mengzhou (representing Zhang Wenbo), Lu Shuchen, and others – about ten people in total. Qin Xiqing, General Manager of the Money Industry Joint Reserve, attended as an observer. Shao Yanshan chaired the meeting, and Secretary Ge Huaiqing recorded the minutes.

Reported Matters. After the formalities, the chairman first reported on the resolutions of the previous meeting: The letter from the Issuance Preparation and Management Committee was approved. The Finance Ministry's reply was approved. The Central Bank Unrestrictedly Recovers Old Subsidiary Coins at the Stipulated Price Until Completion; Various Provinces Are in Great Need of New Coins and Are Rushing to Mint Them 100

The Central Mint, in accordance with Article 6 of the Subsidiary Coinage Regulations, "The old general subsidiary coins shall be recovered, destroyed, and reminted by the Ministry of Finance, but within the prescribed time limit, they shall still be allowed to be used at market prices. The above measures and time limits shall be determined by the Ministry of Finance by order," has entrusted the Central Bank to recover miscellaneous old subsidiary coins. It has signed recovery contracts with the Shanghai Electric Tramway Company, the China General Omnibus Company, and the French Water and Electricity Company, and has also set up retail outlets to recover them. The old coins that have been recovered are temporarily stored in the factory for melting and refining, and then reminted into new coins. Although the factory is rushing to mint new coins day and night, the demand from various provinces is urgent, so they are still continuing to rush to mint them. As for miscellaneous old subsidiary coins, the Central Bank will definitely recover them without restriction until they are all recovered from the market.
