The Judicial Yuan Explains That Dividend Rights Expire If Not Claimed; Requests a Five-Year Limit; The Benefits Belong to the Company's Property 109

The Judicial Yuan recently issued Interpretation No. 1476 regarding the time limit for shareholders to claim dividends and bonuses, replying to the Executive Yuan that "Regarding the question of whether Article 126 of the Civil Code applies, please investigate and interpret it." The Council of Unification and Interpretation of Laws and Decrees of this court has resolved that if shareholders do not claim the dividends and bonuses to be distributed by the company each year after receiving the company's notice, or if they change their address without reporting it to the company in accordance with the regulations, causing the company's notice to be undeliverable, it is all their own fault. If five years have passed since the date the right to claim could be exercised and no claim has been made, in accordance with the provisions of Article 126 of the Civil Code, it should be considered that the right to claim has expired due to the statute of limitations, and any claim made after five years can be rejected. The benefits obtained from refusing to pay naturally belong to the company's property. The reply is hereby sent to you for your information. This is a notice."

County: Promoting Properly Managed Rice Seedlings to Control Rice Stem Borers 112

The Shanghai County's rice stem borer control campaign involved a meeting of district heads convened by the county government, which decided to promote properly managed rice seedlings. The method involves arranging the rice paddies in a square shape, with a four-meter perimeter without restrictions, and leaving walkways on both sides for egg removal. All egg masses found on the rice seedlings should be picked off and burned. All rice straw owned by farmers should be used as soon as possible, and any leftovers should be burned immediately to kill the stem borers lurking inside. Those that must be retained should improve storage methods to prevent the borers from escaping. Now that the planting season has arrived, each district has notified township chiefs to inform each Bao chief to promote trial implementation.

Page 11

Cold and Hot Weather: Early Crops Expected to Fail; Shanghai Grain Stocks Accumulate, Market Prices Contract 113

At this time of year, when spring and summer intersect, the weather alternates between cold and hot. According to reports from the municipal agricultural authorities, there were initial hopes for good harvests of spring crops such as soybeans, wheat, and rapeseed. However, due to this abnormal weather, the prospects for a good harvest are uncertain. Currently, the wheat and rapeseed are in the flowering stage, so the impact is still small. If the weather remains the same for another week, then a poor spring harvest will be inevitable. Furthermore, according to news from the grain industry, rice prices in Shanghai have been declining in recent days due to sluggish sales from out-of-town merchants, leading to an increase in rice stocks. In previous years, rice prices would inevitably rise during this lean season, but this year, they are contracting, which shows how deeply the economic downturn is affecting society. This has a serious impact on the agricultural economy.

Public Bus: Case of a Policeman Run Over and Killed; Driver Sentenced to Five Months; Appeal Rejected 115

Fu Yu, a policeman from the Hengfeng Road Police Station of the Shanghai Municipal Police Department, a 33-year-old native of Shandong, was ordered by his superior on February 8th to deliver official documents to the headquarters by bicycle and return to the station. While passing the entrance of the Xihai Grand Theater at Xinzha Road and Chibang Road, a British-owned Route 10 public bus, number 15041, driven by Wang Jinfang, came speeding towards him. Due to reckless driving, Wang knocked down and ran over Officer Fu, killing him. After an investigation by the relevant patrol station and the Hengfeng Road Police Station, the patrol station surprisingly did not prosecute Wang Jinfang. However, Director Cai of the Municipal Police Department believed that this matter involved a life, and that Wang Jinfang's culpability should be investigated according to the law in order to ensure fairness. Therefore, he appointed the department's legal counsel, lawyer Zhan Jifeng, as the agent for Officer Fu's family to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, with an attached civil suit seeking compensation of 2,800 yuan in national currency for damages. As a result of the trial, Wang Jinfang was sentenced to five months in prison, and the civil suit was transferred to the Civil Division. Wang, dissatisfied with the judgment, hired a lawyer to appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. Lawyer Zhan also appeared in court on behalf of the family. The Second Branch of the High Court recently announced its judgment, rejecting Wang Jinfang's appeal.

Yang Dize and Brothers Return from Exploration of Xikang; Collect Various Specimens of Rare Birds and Animals; Discover a Lake at 12,000 Feet; Eyewitnessing Beautiful Scenery Along the Way Beyond Words 116

The Continental News reports that the well-known American-Chinese Yang Dize and his brothers left Shanghai last August on behalf of the California Academy of Biological Sciences in San Francisco to collect specimens for the museum, with funding provided by Mr. Poth of that city. They have now completed their work and returned to Shanghai. A reporter from the Continental News visited the Yang residence yesterday afternoon (the 9th) for an interview. Mr. Yang eagerly recounted his experiences, saying that the beautiful scenery and wonders witnessed were beyond words. The journey involved one or two dangerous incidents, but the life experience and accomplishments were extremely worthwhile. The two brothers, after bidding farewell to their friends in Shanghai last summer, went to Dajianlu. The ones from New York are slightly different in shape from the Tibetans, and their reproductive abilities are declining significantly. These people are quite suspicious of travelers. The team stayed until the danger had passed before leaving. Then they returned to Dajianlu and advanced to the Minya Konka (transliteration) mountain range, where the scenery was excellent. They stayed there for three months, engaging in collecting. Many beasts were seen, among which the blue sheep were abundant, with more than 2,000 heads seen. Their footprints extended over a hundred square miles, making it one of the richest animal-producing areas in western China. One of the most interesting discoveries of the team was a lake at a high altitude of 12,000 feet, with cliffs as high as 20,000 feet next to it. The beauty of the scene was truly rare. Harden Brock also accompanied them, and he stayed with the team for several months, achieving much. The entire team set off in August, arriving in Dajianlu in western Sichuan in October. After completing their base, they climbed over mountains and crossed ridges, traveling for five days, arriving at Tongyu (transliteration) northeast of Dajian (transliteration), which is on the upper reaches of the Tong River (transliteration). No specimen collectors had ever been there, so the team was almost the first to arrive. They stayed for more than ten days, gaining much. Then they heard that bandits were gathering 20 miles away, very close, and could be seen with binoculars. The team had very few bullets, but decided to stay and help the people resist the bandits, because if they retreated for fear of danger, they would be looked down upon by the people. The residents of this place were said to be descendants of those who had been expelled from Tibet a hundred years ago, and were rarely seen. It was difficult to find food there, and the team members often relied on blue sheep to fill their stomachs. Afterwards, because they had obtained enough, they went to the Muli (transliteration) territory, and then met General Yang Ren'an (transliteration) of the Nanjing government, who allowed them to travel together in the Yi district. The team stayed on the border of Sichuan and Yunnan for a long time. On the way, they heard rumors of bandit troubles around Dajianlu, so they were worried about the many valuable specimens stored there. Then they returned there, packed everything up, and prepared to return. They suddenly abandoned some luggage. This trip obtained many bird and animal specimens, which will be shipped to the California Academy of Biological Sciences in a few days. Some of them will be given to Mr. Poth of San Francisco. Mr. Yang also brought back two Tibetan dogs and two monkeys.

Tenants of Yuanjili, Tangshan Road, File Lawsuit Requesting Rent Reduction; Court Adjourns Hearing the Previous Day; Judgment Scheduled for the 14th 117

The houses in the Yuanjili area of Tangshan Road in Hongkou were built by the Real Estate Department of the Siming Bank. Recently, 102 tenants, including Zhou Yansheng, have jointly hired three lawyers, Jiang Baoli, Jiang Pingfan, and Peng Xuehai, to file a lawsuit with the Civil Division of the First Special Court against Cheng Lansun, the legal representative of the Siming Bank, requesting a rent reduction. The reasons stated were roughly as follows: Since the "January 28th" Incident, Shanghai's economy has declined to an extreme point, and real estate values ​​everywhere have naturally decreased. Therefore, many landlords have voluntarily reduced rents. The defendant's houses not only have not been reduced, but have even increased rents by one or two yuan per month. The plaintiffs are suffering, so they specifically request legal assistance to reduce the monthly rent by 40% from August 1935 to July of this year, based on the original rent. According to Article 44 of the Civil Code, parties may petition the court to increase or decrease rent based on fluctuations in the market value of real estate. The court approved the petition. The previous day, Judge Huang Risheng heard the case in Civil Court Twelve. The courtroom was filled with tenants who came to observe the proceedings, while the defendant's side also hired lawyer Dai Xuzhai to defend them, refusing to reduce the rent. Judge Huang ordered the arguments in the case to be closed and scheduled the judgment for the 14th.

They rushed to the location, confiscated a handbag full of red pills. The Public Works Department filed a public indictment according to Article 257, Section 2 of the Criminal Code, for the crime of selling the drug "red pills." The defendants Zhao Li, represented by lawyer Fan Gang, and Shi Zhaoxiang's attorney requested bail. The court declared that selling red pills was punishable by death according to law and refused to grant bail. Inland River Steamboat Association: Sends Telegram to Zhejiang Construction Department Requesting Exemption from Fuel Storage 121

Recently, the Inland River Steamboat Association of Shanghai has received reports from members operating in Zhejiang province that the Wuxing Second District Ship Management Office is forcing shipping companies to store fuel. Yesterday, the association sent a telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department requesting consideration of the shipping companies' difficulties and exemption from fuel storage. The original telegram is as follows: "Respectfully to Wu Junjian, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, Hangzhou: Recently, we have received reports from members operating in Zhejiang province stating that the Wuxing Zhejiang Second District Ship Management Office recently drafted seven measures for shipping companies in the Lake District to store fuel and attached a guarantee form, forcing shipping companies to sign it. They also claimed that it was being handled according to your instructions, requiring reporting within three days. At a time when the shipping industry is declining, the Ship Management Office is not thinking about ways to protect shipping companies, but is instead arbitrarily drafting impractical fuel storage measures, using administrative power and falsely using your name to force shipping companies to sign, which is a stain on official integrity. We are reporting this and requesting relief. The issue of shipping companies storing fuel was originally for emergency needs. However, since the opening of highways in various parts of the two Zhejiang provinces, the inland river shipping industry has declined drastically. In recent months, the prices of both coal and diesel fuel have soared. Shipping companies are still buying fuel on credit for daily needs. How can they have the ability to store more? We sent a telegram to you in April reporting our difficulties, which was approved. However, the Inland River Shipping Industry Association believes that the inland river shipping environment is deteriorating daily, and there are still problems with the daily fuel requirements. We have the will to serve the country, but we are unable to store fuel. The Second District Shipping Office drafted measures to force shipping companies to sign. After reviewing the proposed measures, each of them increases the burden on shipping companies. Once implemented, it will be equivalent to cutting off the livelihood of our shipping industry. All members of the association are firmly opposed to the above storage measures. In this day and age when strong neighbors are pressing on the border and the country is in dire straits, caring for the people and honest governance are the urgent measures to save the country. There is no reason to disturb the people in order to prepare for national defense. The association believes that this matter concerns the survival of the industry, and that the actions of the Ship Management Office are harmful to the country and the people. For the sake of protecting your good reputation, we cannot remain silent. We respectfully report our business difficulties and hope that you will understand. This is in the public interest. Signed, Han Yimin, Chairman of the Shanghai Inland River Steamboat Association."

Yicheng Exchange Shop: Closes After Operating for Over 30 Days 122

Similar Situation to Mei Hua Bank; Creditors Sue Manager for Fraud

The Yicheng Exchange Shop on Beijing Road was established in March of this year by Qiu Zuxian and others, with a capital of only a few thousand yuan. However, since its opening, business has been poor. Thus, it closed down on the evening of April 9th, just over 30 days after opening. For a circulating financial exchange shop to open for only a little over a month and then close is a rare occurrence, similar to the case of the Mei Hua Bank on Jiujiang Road closing just 19 days after opening. Recently, 22 creditors of the exchange shop, including Hong Bingquan, Yu Rongxing, Chen Laisheng, Xu Zhizhu, and Chen Yaoting, stated that the shop's actions were actually a sham to absorb deposits and take all of the plaintiffs' hard-earned money, which constituted fraud and theft. They jointly hired lawyers to file a lawsuit against the exchange shop's manager Qiu Zuxian, assistant manager Wu Zhengyun, and accountant Jiang Bochuan, in accordance with Article 339 of the Criminal Code, with the First Special Court. In addition to requesting severe punishment according to the law, they also filed a civil suit requesting the recovery of deposits totaling 9,719 yuan. The previous afternoon, the court summoned the defendants. Only Qiu Zuxian, represented by lawyer Lin Yingqing, appeared in court, requesting a postponement. The court ordered the case to be rescheduled for further questioning.

Yi Yuan Rubber Factory Closes; Debts Exceed 300,000 126

Moved from Hong Kong to Shanghai, Operating for 10 Years; Affected by Market, Has Announced Liquidation

The Shanghai Yi Yuan Rubber Factory, located at No. 920, Tangshan Road, has announced its closure due to years of declining business, resulting in financial difficulties. Accountant Chen Riping and lawyer Lu Xingyuan have been appointed for liquidation. The information is provided below:

Factory Summary: The factory was first established in Hong Kong and then moved to Shanghai, with its address at No. 920, Tangshan Road. It has a history of ten years. The manager is He Huishu, a native of Guangdong. The factory's business was initially thriving, but in the past three years, it has been affected by the dumping of foreign rubber products. At the same time, the market has been declining daily. Each year, the business has lost 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. Until recently, it became difficult to maintain its business due to financial difficulties, and it was forced to announce its closure.

Popular Sales of New Interpretation of the Civil Procedure Law 133

Since the implementation of the New Civil Procedure Law on July 1 last year, although there have been many publications and treatises in the market, there are still few that focus on the interpretation of the righteous principles. Therefore, in compiling this book, in addition to explaining the meaning of each legal provision, it is also necessary to repeatedly cite and connect all the provisions of the Civil Procedure Law and related laws to achieve the effect of convenient use and doubling the efficiency. Legal scholar Zai Jixian, recognizing the social need for this book, compiled this book according to the above method, and it was reviewed and revised by Guo Wei, the current president of the Jiangdu District Court. The entire book consists of two volumes, totaling more than 500,000 words, and sells for 2.88 yuan. Since its publication, the supply has fallen short of demand, and the second reprint is about to be sold out. Its content and structure are indeed the only works of modern times. It is currently sold by the Shanghai Lawyers Association at No. 57 Beile Road in the French Concession.

Wife's Infidelity and Scandalous Reputation; Gong Yaoqing Leaves a Note and Drowns Himself; Sends a Letter to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Requesting Retrieval and Burial of the Body; Suicide Is the Act of the Weak; Why Did Gong Yaoqing Take His Own Life? 135

The Tongren Fuyuan Branch of the French Concession received a letter the day before yesterday from the post office, signed by Gong Yaoqing, stating that he had committed suicide by drowning due to marital discord, and requested the retrieval and burial of his body. The letter to the branch is recorded as follows: "My suicide is indeed a family misfortune. If I could have endured, I would never have resorted to this course of action. Moreover, I work for a certain company and earn more than 20 yuan a month, which is enough to maintain a small family. How could I know that my wife, He, would not care at all and would borrow indiscriminately, even pawning and mortgaging everything? That was still the limit. Unexpectedly, recently a change has occurred, and she has become acquainted with Xu Qingfa. She does not return day or night, as if they were husband and wife. Seeing this situation, I am ashamed and have no interest in being a human being. Being in this world is just suffering. In addition, yesterday my wife even deliberately made a scene at the company, demanding money, causing a great disturbance and damaging my reputation. My colleagues laughed at me. After a brief argument, I was humiliated by her. Resentful, I had nowhere to vent my anger, so I had to drown myself to end my remaining life. If anyone finds my body, please provide a coffin for burial. I am wearing a thread-lined jacket and pants, black socks, and slightly broken leather shoes. There is a 20-cent auxiliary coin in my pocket. Please also notify the rescue bureau to pay attention. I would be grateful." Attached was a letter to his wife: "Wife Xuezhen, today I bid you farewell forever. See how you enjoy your life alone. How can you bear to treat your husband so ruthlessly? I have nothing more to say to you now, only to sacrifice my life before you. However, after my death, I want you to think about whether I have done anything wrong to you. You probably don't understand, and there is also your cousin. Since we have lived together, I believe I have not treated you badly. As for money, although it is not abundant, it is enough to support the family. You still say in front of others that your husband supports you. Alas, you are embarrassing me. What benefit is there to you? As the saying goes, 'Marry a dog, follow the dog; marry a pig, follow the pig.' You should have conjugal harmony. Even if you are dissatisfied, you can always get a divorce. Don't do such shameless things in secret. You also have to think about where to put your husband's face and how to face relatives and friends. What you have done, you still don't realize. You don't return day or night. I don't know what you are busy with. Everyone goes to shows, but no one is as shameless as you. For example, a few days ago, you told me you were going to your sister's place in Hongkou. I, as your husband, didn't stop you. How could I know your words were still lies, and you went to the Oriental Hotel with your lover? At that time, I couldn't sternly tell you why you didn't return. How can you be worthy of your husband in this respect? When you came back the next day, you were still being unreasonable, treating your husband as a fool, and advising you with kind words, considering our marriage, but you still wanted to quarrel with me, acting arrogantly. Aren't you clearly deceiving me? As the ancients said, 'Family scandals should not be made public.' I am your husband, and I don't want to tell others, but you have the nerve to say that having lovers in Shanghai is okay. Your neighbors and teachers can testify to this. According to you, there is no relationship. Still, I provide you with clothes and food. So heartless. No wonder your cousin scolded you as inhuman. You said the more you are controlled, the more you are like this. Now I will let you go. Staying in the world is just anger. Let you be free and unrestrained. As for the company, since I can sacrifice my life today, I will not spare anything else. I have already sent another letter. You can take all the items and sell them as you please. This is the end for us. No more words. Finished. Written by your deceased husband, Gong Yaoqing." After receiving the letter, the branch notified the rescue bureau to order the rescue boats to pay attention to retrieving the body from the river.

Reply from the Shanghai District Court to the Lawyers Association 138

The Shanghai Lawyers Association requested the Shanghai District Court to improve the procedures for reporting to the court for trial, rescheduling hearings, and executing seizures. The court has now issued a reply, which is recorded below. Reply from the Jiangsu Shanghai District Court, one case. The request for adopting and improving the procedures for reporting to the court for trial, rescheduling hearings, and executing seizures has been received and approved. The points requested for adoption and improvement have already been implemented by this court. The analysis and explanation are as follows: Reporting to the court. This is related to the volume of the courtroom. The size and volume of this court's courtrooms vary. If reporting to the court is uniformly implemented, it will inevitably be crowded and hinder the trial of cases. The parties to the case can indicate the time in the registration book, which is sufficient to determine whether they arrived on time. Specifying the date of the continued hearing in court. This court has always handled it this way. However, there are exceptions in cases where it is necessary to entrust the investigation of evidence or investigate reference files, and other circumstances. Seizure cases. Each clerk in this court's execution office schedules three or four seizure cases every day. As for the method of execution, each is handled at the discretion of the situation at the time. Seizure of movable property worth less than one hundred yuan. This court has already implemented this in handling this type of case. The bailiff will estimate the value at that time. For the sake of caution, the valuation situation must be submitted to the executing judge for approval before notifying the creditor to take it over. In summary, the above four points have been handled by this court without any hindrance. You are hereby notified. This order.

General Manager of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory Cai Shengbo Sued; Court Will Continue Hearing Today 144

After the government designated blue robes and black jackets as formal attire, they have been worn for weddings, funerals, and gatherings. Since the creation of group weddings, they have also been used as formal attire for the groom. As a result, silk and satin companies have been vying for business. The Meiya Silk Weaving Factory at No. 140 Tianjin Road and its branch store, Kai Li Silk and Satin Company at No. 765 Jing'an Temple Road, have taken advantage of the opportunity to advertise their production of formal attire, claiming that they have been approved by the Social Affairs Bureau. A certain Standard Silk and Satin Company, separated by a wall of profit, is also located at No. 763 Jing'an Temple Road, engaged in the same silk and satin business, and also making various formal attires. Due to business competition, they have ended up in litigation. The court held a hearing on this case a few days ago. The plaintiff is Lin Zhixiang, the owner of Standard Silk and Satin Company, and the defendants are Cai Shengbo, the general manager of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory and chairman of Kai Li Silk and Satin Company, and Gao Shiheng, the manager of Kai Li Company. According to the plaintiff's statement of reasons for the lawsuit, Li Li Company sells silk and satin and also makes formal attire. It once published an advertisement stating that it provides free production of the blue robe and black jacket standard formal attire approved by this association. Cai Shengbo and Gao Shiheng envied the plaintiff's business and damaged it by falsely accusing the plaintiff of counterfeiting and secretly presenting a request to the Social Affairs Bureau to stop it, attempting to obstruct the business. They then publicly hung the instructions obtained from the Bureau at the entrance of the Kai Li Company on Jing'an Temple Road. Under the instructions, they added an advertisement with the words "Purchase Meiya standard formal attire. Please pay attention to counterfeiting and shoddy goods masquerading as genuine." publicly damaging the plaintiff's reputation. The formal attire approved by the Social Affairs Bureau is based on silk-woven blue robes and black jackets as the standard. Any manufacturer can weave according to this standard. The Meiya Silk Factory and Kai Li Company operated by the defendants do not have the exclusive right to weave or produce them, and the term "Social Affairs Bureau approved standard formal attire" is not a special trademark. The defendants have no right to interfere with the plaintiff's advertisement for making "Social Affairs Bureau approved standard formal attire." Now, they have spread these words to the public, pointing fingers and damaging the reputation of the plaintiff, thus jointly committing the crime of defamation under the criminal law and filing a civil lawsuit requesting the court to order the defendants to publish an apology advertisement on the cover of the "Shen Bao" and "Xin Wen" newspapers. Judge Yang Qianchang is handling this case in the Criminal Division Two. The plaintiff has commissioned lawyers Zhu Chengxun and Xue Jiaqi to appear in court, while the defendant Gao Shiheng has appeared, and Cai Shengbo has not appeared due to other matters. The defendant has commissioned Chen Tingrui to appear and defend. According to the defendant's defense, the production of formal attire has been approved by the Social Affairs Bureau, and Meiya has been entrusted with handling it in Shanghai. It has been ordered that Meiya products can be used for all formal attire. Therefore, the plaintiff is deliberately interfering with the business and now filing a criminal lawsuit, which is unreasonable. During the statement, the plaintiff gesticulated and lost the dignity of the court. The judge reprimanded him to correct his behavior. The plaintiff replied that the standard formal attire is the blue robe and black jacket, and the Social Affairs Bureau has approved that it is a silk fabric. Any manufacturer can produce it according to this standard. How can the defendant monopolize it? Moreover, they spread words publicly, deliberately hanging the Social Affairs Bureau's note on the doorway and adding annotations, which clearly defames the plaintiff's reputation and constitutes a crime. Judge Yang then said that both parties are legitimate merchants. This is a trivial matter and should be resolved out of court. The hearing was adjourned to next Monday (today).

Publishing World 145

The Imparting of Chinese Philosophy to the West: The Book of Changes (I Ching) is an extremely systematic philosophical work with a long history, revered by sages and saints. Many people dismiss it as being akin to divination, but this is not the case. The principles of the Book of Changes are profound and encompass everything. Although one might want to explore them, it is difficult to find a path. Mr. Shen Zhongtao of Shaoxian deeply understands the importance of I Ching studies, so in his spare time, he buries himself in research, using his new ideas to prove the effectiveness of the I Ching with science. His forthcoming new works, "I Ching Hexagrams and Science" and "Chinese-English I Ching," are both in English. The content includes mathematics, physics, logic, astronomy, etc., with fifty to sixty illustrations, each with detailed explanations. The theory is thorough, like sifting sand to find gold, making the mysteries of ancient philosophy suddenly clear. Scholars who read this will not only learn the principles of science but also gain insight into the gateway to philosophy. It is truly essential reading. Currently, universities and libraries in various countries that have obtained these books have praised them in unison, considering them a unique and brilliant contribution to the world of philosophy. The price for each of the above two books is $2.50. Published by the China New Education Society, Lude Runfang, Avenue Edward VII, Shanghai. Distributed by Biefa Foreign Firm, Nanjing Road.

Publication of the Famous Work "Adventures of a Wooden Puppet in the Philippines": The illustrated full-length novel "Adventures of a Wooden Puppet in the Philippines" is one of the world's famous children's literature works, comparable to "The Adventures of Pinocchio." It tells the story of a wooden puppet's adventurous journey into Africa to explore its wonders, experiencing all kinds of dangers, humorous and strange encounters. He goes from being a servant to an emperor, and from an emperor to a slave, finally escaping from this dark Africa. It is full of thrills, humor, and educational value, suitable for both children and adults. Original work by the Italian Xue Lu Kunni, translated by Jiang Manru, revised by Wang Tiran. The translation is extremely clear and lively, and the eighty illustrations further enhance interest. Printed in regular script, two hundred pages thick, actual price 70 cents. Published by the Dushu Jie Bookstore, No. 31 Yüshenfu Road, Shanghai. Available for sale at Shenghuo Bookstore, Kaiming Bookstore, Author's Publishing House, Shidai Book Company, Shanghai Magazine Company, and the distribution departments of Dagong Pao in various regions. For direct purchases from the bookstore, postage is waived for out-of-town orders, and payment is collected upon delivery in Shanghai.

Weather Report 147

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Northern China will be cloudy with sand and strong northerly to westerly winds. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River will change from cloudy to clear with local rain. The lower reaches and this area will be cloudy with rain or drizzle. The East China Sea will have rain and northeasterly to southeasterly winds. The area around Taiwan will be cloudy with gentle northerly to easterly winds. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai was 64.4 degrees at its highest and 55.6 degrees at its lowest. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 84.2 degrees, and the lowest was 65.3 degrees.

Impressions of Shanghai 156

— Li Huitang

At 4:00 PM on May 2nd, the French postal ship, the Aramis, slowly moved and sailed south to Wusongkou. Our team members all took a deep breath of fresh air, expressing a comfortable pleasure. This was not because we disliked Shanghai and wanted to leave as soon as possible. However, we were indeed a bit tired of the ball games and the ball atmosphere. It was naturally a joyful thing to leave quickly and go to the sea to breathe some fresh air. Half a month ago, the World Games football preliminary selection was held in Hong Kong. At the same time, our Hong Kong team was rushing to finish the annual competition. As a result, there were overlapping matches, with four or five matches every week. After the selection results were out, our spirits were exhausted, our muscles were fatigued, and our interest had cooled to zero. We really had a "seeing the ball makes us sick" mentality. Then, we were ordered by the National Sports Association to come to Shanghai to perform in the exhibition matches. We felt tired and exhausted, but how could we refuse the association's summons?

As a tired army running to Shanghai to meet new horses, although we were confident that we had done our best and worked hard to the extreme, we knew that it was impossible for us to bring out our full skills in this environment. Really, in these matches, no one had a brilliant performance. This abnormal display was something we expected. Therefore, we all hope that people who love us will not be too harsh on our dissatisfaction this time.

The most unfortunate thing was that on April 28th, our eleven pairs of hairy legs were too disappointing and could not defeat the West League team, causing thousands of fans who "loved us deeply and hoped for the best" to go home disappointed. This is the biggest regret of our trip to Shanghai. In fact, the outcome of a ball game is the most unpredictable thing. According to my experience, first-class teams in England often lose to third-class teams. Moreover, the fighting power of the West League team is not much better than ours. Although winning or losing is a natural principle, one or two games are not certain. Unless the two teams play ten or eight times, the goddess of luck will not easily play tricks and prove who is superior and who is inferior.

Because of this defeat, it caused a storm in the city. The criticisms in the newspapers and the criticisms of the fans were varied, giving us a great lesson and a deep impression. This has to be said to be a great gift from this failure. I often feel that the criticisms of our country's press or fans are often biased or inappropriate. They really attach too much importance to the words "win or lose." When they win the ball, no matter how bad the performance is, the whole team will surely win praise, saying it like a cascade of flowers. When they lose the ball, the opposite is true. They don't investigate the reasons for the failure at all, and they don't understand the difficulties of the failure at all. In fact, the same square toes, the same circle, and the same blood, who doesn't want to perform their best when they get to the stadium? We have a vital stake in it, who would willingly abandon themselves? However, sometimes "if the horse doesn't go forward, it's not because it dares to go backward." It is only because of special reasons that the performance is not satisfactory. Regarding this review, I want to use the space here to briefly explain the truth.

A newspaper said that "when I kicked the penalty kick, I didn't understand the rules after hitting the post, and I added another kick." This is too wronged. If I don't even understand this simple rule, then what qualifications do I have to be a captain and referee? The fact is that the ball bounced back from the post too quickly, so I couldn't avoid it, so I touched it and fouled. How could I have the intentional intention to add another kick? This kind of record is untrue and is proof of the reporter's superficial knowledge, which is an obstacle to the development of sports.

There is also an unknown "Old He Jun" who earnestly gave me instructions and enlightenment in his report. I always welcome people's sincere advice to me, but what he said also needs to be explained. He said that the performance of the center back line in the first half was not good, and the captain turned a blind eye in the second half and did not replace others. In fact, that day was a British game and was not allowed to be replaced. This is where he didn't know the truth and wasted his argument. He also said that "the old generals Cao Guicheng and Li Guowei can no longer be used." Cao and Li's performance that day was indeed abnormal, but every player has a day of abnormality, so how can we observe the superiority or inferiority with one or two games and make a definite decision? Besides, the word "old general" can still be said to be in Cao Guizhen, but Li Guowei is only twenty-three this year, so is he considered old? Guowei's average performance in Hong Kong is quite good. Both Chinese and Western newspapers believe that he is the best left center back. "It should not be used again in the future." This sentence may be inappropriate. In short, I said above that everyone felt too tired this time, and the interest was not strong. Although every game did not give up the heart of eating, it was only a forced effort to support the spirit and exhaustion. It is most unfair to draw a conclusion under these circumstances. There is also the "×× Weekly" that has always attacked me, who puts the failure of Dao Jue on my personal head and adds other kinds of demeaning remarks, saying that I am old and useless, and should not be selected. It should have everything, attacking with all its strength. I have no common hatred with them, and I don't know why. Fortunately, this kind of black newspaper is just to win the sympathy of the lower class, and there is no value. In fact, a penalty kick, if you can't kick it in, it won't necessarily affect the final situation of winning or losing. But it's a common thing to not be able to kick a penalty kick, and it's not worth making a fuss about it. The best shooters in the world sometimes lose their feet, not to mention our lower-level generations. As for "old" and "degeneration," I am not a superman, and this is something that will come sooner or later. How can I be so stupid? It is only a pity that they attack so hard, but the station does not work. The association turned a deaf ear and put the responsibility of the captain on my shoulders. Then how can I be too old, or not at all useful? I still remember that in the last performance match in Hong Kong, I was blessed to score five goals, and I got good criticisms from newspapers and fans. Today is only half a month away, and degeneration will never come so quickly. I insist on my own self-confidence, saying that I am not too old or not at all useless.

If I were not sick, I would have published this article to the public to show the truth of the facts. I did not intend to vent my anger or defend the team members. In fact, we have exhausted our blood, spirit and energy, and we have a clear conscience. People's arguments are about right and wrong and the victory or defeat of the ball game. How can we care so much? Our ten-day stay in Shanghai has given us the impression that the people of Shanghai have the same mentality as their compatriots in other places. What is this mentality? This is "the victory or defeat of the ball game, love and hate follow," and the word "victory" is too heavily biased. Therefore, we are not at all pessimistic about our ball game failure. We see that the criticisms of the newspapers and the arguments of the people are inappropriate, and that the support of the fans is not in accordance with justice, and then we feel the hopelessness of our country's sports future.

The National Children's Painting Exhibition is scheduled to begin on June 6th at the city center sports field. During the opening period, children's painting performances will also be held to allow them to demonstrate their skills on the spot. School Investigation

An Overview of the German School in Shanghai (4) 176

— Hu Zuyin

The focus of the school's moral education is to cultivate national spirit. The first step in cultivating national spirit is to implement national character teaching, that is, to use materials needed by the people of the country as much as possible in language, literature, history, and geography. At the same time, the school often reminds children of the development and success of their nation, so that children can develop a noble national spirit in a subtle way. For example, in this decision, Germany announced the abandonment of the Locarno Treaty and sent troops to station in the Rhineland demilitarized zone. The history and geography teachers of the school used slide projectors to show the children about the geography, customs, and human feelings of the Rhine River and nearby areas so that these children in foreign countries could also understand the situation of their motherland and make their patriotism arise spontaneously.

Another method used by the school to cultivate national spirit is to train children's physique. A healthy physique is the foundation of national spirit. Although the school does not have perfect gymnasium facilities, it actively trains children's physique. The school usually has five classes every morning, from 8:30 to 12:30. There are no formal lessons for each grade in the afternoon, but students of all grades must take turns coming to school to participate in fitness exercises. Boys in each grade take turns coming to school three times in the afternoon every week to exercise their physique: girls also have to come to school in the same way, but one or two of the fitness exercises are changed to needlework. Other group fitness activities, such as sports meets, excursions, and mountain climbing, are also often held.

6. Hitler Youth League

German youth training has been quite famous in the past. Since Hitler came to power, the work of youth training has been carried out more actively. Hitler has now concentrated the national youth training work under the guidance of the government to train uncivilized citizens for the country. The Hitler Youth League is one of the ways in German youth training. The German School in Shanghai also has the organization of the Hitler Youth League. Now I will briefly introduce the organization and activities of the Hitler Youth League.

The Hitler Youth League can be divided into two groups according to the age of the children: the first group is the young children's team, which children from ten to fourteen years old join; the second group is the youth team, which young people from fifteen to eighteen years old join. On the girls' side, there are also similar two teams. The first team is the girls' team, which girls from ten to fourteen years old join; the first team is the Federal German Girls' Team, which girls from fifteen to twenty-one years old join. The organization of the group is like this: There are fifteen entries called a squad, fifty people called a company, one hundred and fifty people called a battalion, six hundred people called a district team, and a certain number of district teams can form a district team, and a certain number of district teams can form a regiment. There are currently twenty-five Hitler Youth League regiments in Germany; the number of members in each regiment is about 75,000 for men and an equal number for women. The Youth League of the German School in Shanghai is also directly under the command of Hitter. The regiment's flag, uniform, etc. are all stipulated by Hitler.

The purpose of Hitler's Youth League training is to develop a healthy personality and a sense of duty. Therefore, the training of the Youth League includes fitness exercises, boxing, shooting, field camping, reconnaissance, hiking, mountain climbing, etc. Special attention is also paid to spiritual training. It is automatic for German male and female students to join the Hitler Youth League, not reluctant. However, once you join, you must accept strict training. Last summer, Hitler summoned the domestic and foreign youth groups in Germany to hold centralized training; the Youth League of the German School in Shanghai also sent representatives to participate in the country. (End)

Spring and Autumn

The Goat's Fault 177

— (Kang Dun)

There is a popular folk tale in Abyssinia:

One day, a pair of leopards went out and left their cub in the cave. An elephant broke into the leopard's den, killed the cub, and savored its tender flesh. The leopard's neighbor went to report:

"Your beloved son has been killed."

"Who killed it?"

"An elephant killed it."

"Ah! An elephant? An elephant wouldn't kill my cub. It must have been that hateful goat that killed it."

"No, it was definitely an elephant."

"I'm telling you, it must have been the goat that killed my son, not anyone else." After saying this, it leapt up and devoured the goat to vent its hatred for the death of its cub.

Originally, the leopard knew that its son had been killed by the elephant, but because it was not a match for the giant elephant, it had to vent its anger on the goat. This is the origin of the idiom "the goat's fault" (It is the foul of the goats).

The current Abyssinia has been defeated. But this time, they will not blame the goat for fearing the giant elephant. After all, they fought to the death with the giant elephant, and although they were defeated, they were still honorable.

30th Anniversary of Joining the Army 178

— Chou Cheng

In the 32nd year of Emperor Guangxu's reign during the Qing Dynasty, Su Fu Jichunjiang, in view of the fact that the practice of recruiting soldiers was too deeply ingrained and unreliable, started conscription in the counties of Su, Song, and Tai. In addition to assigning graduates of the Land Army and Military Preparatory Schools to set up conscription bureaus in various counties of the three prefectures, he also ordered local gentry to carefully draft methods for serving, waiting, and encourage them to persuade. Xu stipulated that if conscripts had important matters at home, acquaintances would help each other to avoid worries at home. After retirement, they would be invited to the upper seat at public banquets to show respect. He also specially composed a farewell song, referring to the example of scholars entering the academy, publicly preparing colorful flags and drums, and the public group school would welcome and send them to the camp. The song said: "Great citizens of the East and West, people like to be soldiers, one son is a soldier, six relatives are honored, walk and send them with joy. There are many good men in Jiangsu, they should enlist together, the military uniform is glorious, and it is a credit to their parents and fame. Last year, the military power shone in Beiyang, and Hejian was used as a drill ground. The two armies fought like facing an enemy, and the dragon flag fluttered in the morning sun. Military officials from various countries came one after another, and the progress was surprising. Newspapers praised them, and the names of the soldiers were spread. Since ancient times, Wu has had many heroes, who regard death as if returning home. Those who start out in the army are noble, and their ambitions will not be violated. You see Zhang Yao and Sun Shao Xiang, how glorious their battle achievements are. If they return with meritorious service in other countries in the future, their bronze statues will stand tall. Soldiers, soldiers, don't waste your time, listen to my conscription song. Soldiers, farmers, industry and commerce are all equal, let's all hold weapons together. The forest of guns and the rain of bullets are not enough to fear, victory lies in harmony, and the heroism in our hearts is now revealed, to protect our beautiful rivers and mountains." Therefore, for a time, the sons of gentry and tribute students broke the old saying that "good iron is not made into nails, and good men are not soldiers," and enlisted one after another, totaling more than 1,500 people. At that time, I was studying at Jiaxing Xiushui School, so I asked for leave to go to Suzhou, pretended to be a native of Wuxian County, and enlisted. In the same year, I was admitted to the Land Army Training School out of 80 people out of 1,500 people, and taught two subjects of academics. After graduation, I was assigned to the first and second standard generals. In the Xinhai Restoration, I followed Governor Cheng Xuelou to attack Ning, and it has been 30 years since then. Among these 1,500 people, many died in battle and of illness, and those who are still alive are scattered in all directions and have changed careers. Now the government is promoting the conscription system again. We can be called the first group of conscripts. Therefore, I initiated the 30th anniversary of joining the army on May 3rd, which was held at Huqiu in Suzhou. Forty people reported, and they talked about their experiences in the past 30 years, which was quite emotional. Several of them had not met for more than 20 years, and they almost did not recognize each other.

Hesitating in the Palm of Your Hand 180

—

Changing Nests of Lovebirds 181

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter One: Sipping Tea and Engaging in Conversation by a Night Window Listening to Rain, Plucking Branches to Admire Their Beauty as Fragrance Flows Through the Flower Lane

Guoqi felt extremely sorry about this matter, thinking that he had kept the person sitting for a while without even offering a cup of hot tea. To make matters worse, he had even splashed mud on them when they left. In any case, he had to return the visit tomorrow, whether it was sunny or raining; he could not miss this opportunity. With this idea in mind, he glanced at the house across the way, where his mother had already retired, and he turned off the lamp to sleep, planning to finish his homework early the next morning so he could leave class early and meet Pingshan. When he woke up in the morning, expecting it to be another rainy day, he was still reluctant to get out of bed. But as he rolled over and sat up, he opened his eyes and saw a golden ray of sunlight on the glass window. The gloom of the past several days vanished completely as he opened his eyes. He washed up, drank tea, and bid farewell to his mother before hurrying out the door. Right next door was someone's vegetable garden, enclosed by earthen walls on two sides and a fence on the other. Many vegetables were planted on the ground, and along the fence were planted a hundred or so slender bamboo stalks. After being soaked by the rain, the bamboo appeared especially verdant in the bright sunlight. He didn't know what kind of small birds they were, but seven or eight of them were flying and chirping on the bamboo branches. In the vegetable garden, a few inches of chives were sparsely emerging, topped with tiny yellow flowers. With just these embellishments, the impression of early spring was quite profound. This was the same road that Guoqi passed every day, but he usually didn't find anything particularly delightful about it. Now, illuminated by the gentle spring light, it felt exceptionally pleasing to the eye. In particular, the southeast wind blowing from the bamboo tips caressed his face without feeling cold at all. This made the air in his chest feel very comfortable to breathe. Although Nanjing City was so grand, on this day, the north of the city was entirely bamboo groves and vegetable and wheat fields. Even though the south of the city was densely populated, ponds and vegetable gardens were everywhere. Guoqi lived in the west of the city, where the streets and alleys were filled with old-style architecture, with roof tiles without eaves covering low, crumbling lime walls. Between every two or three houses, there were always two or three patches of vegetable gardens or a clump of wild bamboo. The narrow alleys were paved with cobblestones, arranged in no particular pattern. In the cracks between the cobblestones or at the foot of the walls, a patch of wild grass leaves or a ring of moss protruded. There were few pedestrians in the alleys, except for women washing clothes in the wild ponds, carrying their laundry baskets. Or peddlers carrying baskets, carrying a load of green vegetables, passing by quickly. With few pedestrians, the sounds of people were also very quiet. Instead, the clatter of silk weaving machines echoed from the workshops, carrying the sound of the looms through the clear sky. Guoqi thought of the lines, "Listening to spring rain overnight in a small building, selling apricot blossoms in a deep lane in the morning," and wondered, if there were a flower seller passing by here at this moment, no matter what kind of flower it was, it would be very poetic. (19)

Short Story

Street Violinist 182

— Xia Fei

It was a twilight evening in late spring, with dense rain falling silently. The metropolis seemed dead, all worldly affairs temporarily at rest.

The surroundings in the room were silent. The damp air was oppressive, making it difficult to breathe. I casually picked up a book to read, but I set it aside without even finishing half a page. I walked to the window and pushed open the glass pane, intending to look out at the streets in the drizzling rain, but the wind blew on my body and the rain splattered on my face. A chilling, dismal feeling crept into my heart like a small brown snake.

Although it was already late spring, the weather seemed stuck in early spring, so cold and gloomy that it was hard to believe it was the season of bright spring and blooming flowers.

I closed the window, went back in, and threw my heavy body into a recliner. An nameless sorrow gripped my heart, making me feel the emptiness and impermanence of life, the meaninglessness and superfluity of everything in the world...

As I was silently tracing the past, savoring the present, and longing for the future, a melancholic melody drifted from the streets in the distance. The sounds, one after another, section after section, entered my ears, causing my nerves to be keenly stimulated, feeling that the trembling tone was telling the misery of life. The sound gradually came closer and became clearer. So I stood up and opened the window, leaning on the windowsill to listen, forgetting the cold, forgetting the rainy night. I only heard the mournful, sorrowful tune, like the cry of apes in a valley, like a widow weeping, sending it over. From each prolonged and trembling cadence, I seemed to see a haggard old man standing under a dim street lamp, or squatting in the dark streets and alleys like a ghost, dragging a lonely shadow, trying to use this single string to express his boundless sorrow, grief, humiliation, anger...

The sound passed, gradually fading into the black night of wind and rain. Only then did I look up in disappointment at the silent street, seeing only the dim streetlights illuminating the wide, flat road. These buildings cast many shadows on the ground, making it seem as if they had gone through a storm under the dim yellow light.

Returning inside, I realized that my clothes and hair were all wet.

That night, I lay in bed, unable to fall asleep, tossing and turning. Although I buried my head deep in the covers and tried to shut out all thoughts to calm my nerves, it didn't work. That melancholic melody, that thin, sallow face, kept circling and appearing in my mind. A feeling of sadness and desolation kept crawling in my heart, like a poisonous snake coiling around my weathered, wounded soul, causing it to ache.

I didn't close my eyes all night, just staring blankly at the ceiling, searching for unrelated memories, until the glass window showed a glimmer of white light.

Since that night, I have heard that mournful, sorrowful tune every night, echoing in my ears. And since that night, I have begun to suffer from severe insomnia.

When a person requests a book, they should have the sharp eyes, agile means, and sacrificial spirit of a hunter, not the leisurely and unhurried attitude of a Mr. Nice Guy. Reading without seeking thorough understanding, thinking that there is inexhaustible love and unlimited heavenly secrets!

The Usefulness of Bedbugs 185

— Zi Ying

Soak bedbugs that have fed fully in vegetable oil until saturated. When someone is burned by fire, take a few drops of the oil and apply it to the wound. After three or four minutes, the pain will stop. Also, for snake bites, apply bedbugs to the wound, and it can heal.

Poor families, who have suffered the harm of bedbugs, may sometimes want to turn around and make use of them.

Demanding 186

— Qiu Jie

When someone possesses something I don't, it's reasonable for me to borrow it from them and return it when I have it myself. However, there are two things that can only be demanded from others and cannot be borrowed. If you say you're borrowing, you will definitely be hated by the other party. What are these two things? They are "tea" and "fire." If you say you're borrowing "tea" (especially from women), it implies flirtatiousness, and borrowing "fire" is taboo in social superstition. The most ridiculous thing is that people clearly spend betrothal gifts and go through all sorts of complicated procedures to marry a woman, but society commonly calls it "demanding a wife." This use of the word "demand" is extremely illogical! Moreover, the women who are married are all young and beautiful, so how can they be called "old women"? It's truly unbelievable!

Fei Xiaolou 187

— Ji Yijie

The famous painter Fei Xiaolou was a person from the Jiaqing and Daoguang periods of the Qing Dynasty. His painted beauties are still praised to this day. People all know that Xiaolou was a famous painter of beauties, but they don't know that his portraits were incredibly lifelike and exquisite, possessing the magic of surpassing nature.

Legend has it that during the Daoguang period of the former Qing Dynasty, there was an uncle of the Emperor who was blind in one eye. He repeatedly hired painters to paint his portrait, but none satisfied him because all the painters simply copied what they saw, failing to conceal his defect. Later, Xiaolou was invited. Xiaolou discreetly learned of the situation and specially painted a picture of a barber cleaning ears. The person in the picture (the Emperor Daoguang's uncle) had one eye slightly closed, as if unable to bear the tickling sensation. It was both realistic and concealed his blindness. The Emperor Daoguang's uncle praised him greatly and gave him generous gifts. Painters like Xiaolou can be said to have come up with an original idea, and his "reputation in painting" has a reason.

Two Other Aliases for Tofu 188

— Yi Ping

It is correct that tofu, known as Chengzhaojun tofu, was invented by Liu An, the King of Huainan. However, besides being called shuru, tofu also has the aliases laiqi and liqi. The name laiqi can be found in "Yu Ji's Writings": "In local language, tofu is called laiqi." The name liqi can be found in Lu You's poem: "Wipe the plate and quickly spread it out; wash the pot and cook liqi." Most likely, laiqi and liqi are simply variations of the same pronunciation! As for the reason why Zhu Xi didn't eat tofu, besides what Chengzhaojun said, it is rumored that Zhu Xi's family sold tofu, and he must have eaten too much of it and didn't want to eat it anymore.

Knowing Without Divination 189

— Yan Dunjin

If you see someone on the street with a toothpick in their mouth, they must have just come out of a restaurant.

If you see someone carrying a hatbox or shoebox in their hand, but their head or feet are already brand new, then the box in their hand must contain an old hat or shoes, without a doubt. (But sometimes the hatbox is empty.)

If you see someone carrying a rolled-up small padded jacket and pants, and their face is glowing, they are most likely coming out of a bathhouse. (For a fee)

— (Xue Wei)

Sweet... Kissing your lover, this taste is the sweetest! Spicy... When your lover asks you to buy a leather coat! High heels... Such a taste is a bit unbearable!

Sour... Often you see your lover kissing another member of the opposite sex. This is the sourest taste!

Bitter... If your lover marries another member of the opposite sex, this taste is the most bitter!
