Economic Special

On Financial Measures During Wartime 192

— Yu Qiong

What will our finances be like during wartime? What kind of measures should be implemented? This has become a problem that must be considered now. Here, I intend to briefly discuss an outline.

What impact will war have on the financial markets? In short, it is the destruction of international and domestic credit. Our problem lies in how to respond to this situation after the destruction of domestic and foreign credit. After the outbreak of war, the first to be affected will undoubtedly be the foreign exchange and securities markets. Once the opportunity arises, foreign capital will inevitably withdraw from our country on a large scale. Foreign property, regardless of whether it is stocks, bonds, real estate, or other investments, will be disposed of and taken back. Foreign banks will inevitably transfer their active assets back to their home countries. As for their stocks, bonds, and discounted notes, they will either be dumped on the market or directly transferred to domestic banks for foreign exchange discounting. The movement of foreign capital will become the first layer of heavy pressure on our foreign exchange and securities markets. Domestically, some capital will inevitably try to escape at the opportunity. Merchants will sell securities, withdraw deposits, and turn to national banks to purchase foreign exchange. The flight of domestic capital will become the second layer of heavy pressure on the foreign exchange and securities markets. Under these circumstances, the securities market will inevitably experience severe turmoil first, and banks will be unable to immediately recover loans to meet customer withdrawals, inevitably leading to widespread insolvency. Money shops will collapse one after another due to banks tightening credit and recalling loans with no place to turn around. National banks will also face an extraordinary crisis, because foreign property is intended to be disposed of and taken back, and some domestic capital is also intended to escape at the opportunity. Foreign property will quickly turn to the Big Three banks to purchase foreign exchange, and people will withdraw deposits from banks and follow suit to the Big Three banks to exchange for foreign exchange. The Big Three's ability to stabilize foreign exchange will face an extraordinary test. Under the current monetary system—the foreign exchange standard—the scramble to purchase foreign exchange is, in fact, no different from a general bank run. Foreign exchange reserves can be exhausted in an instant. Credit panic will become unmanageable. The key to suppressing the turmoil lies in this point.

At this time, the problems are: first, to avoid disruption of the financial markets; second, to ensure the integrity of credit institutions; and third, to preserve foreign exchange reserves. The emergency measures are: first, to avoid disruption of the financial markets, the only way is to order the exchanges to immediately close; second, to ensure the integrity of credit institutions, the only way is to order banks and all monetary institutions to temporarily suspend payments; third, to preserve foreign exchange reserves, the only way is to temporarily implement foreign exchange controls. These three points are the first step in dealing with wartime finance. The closure of the exchanges is an inevitable result of major changes in securities prices. This may happen even before the government orders it, and it will be forced to close first. However, government bonds are the mainstay of exchange trading, and government credit is directly reflected by the exchange. If the exchange is allowed to be forced to close on its own, government credit will inevitably leave a bad impression on the people's minds first. Therefore, the government should take precautions and anticipate that the situation may not be completely controllable. It is better to order it to close in advance than to resort to it as a last resort after the situation has become unmanageable. As for announcing the suspension of payments, the purpose is to ensure the integrity of credit institutions. It should not be a reactive measure, and should not be implemented until banks and money shops have collapsed one after another and the market has become blocked. This problem is also closely related to preserving foreign exchange reserves. If people are allowed to withdraw and deposit freely, they will immediately turn to the Central Bank to purchase foreign exchange after depositing in ordinary banks, or even discount foreign exchange to the Big Three with deposit slips and passbooks from various banks, which is no different from forcing the Big Three to pay foreign exchange with deposits from various banks, and the loss of foreign exchange will be accelerated. Therefore, announcing the suspension of payments is also a measure to preserve foreign exchange reserves. As for foreign exchange controls, it is, in fact, no different from suspending convertibility. Under the current monetary system, although people cannot exchange legal tender for cash at banks, they can exchange it for foreign exchange according to the law, and the Big Three are legally responsible for unlimited supply. If Chinese and foreigners are allowed to freely purchase foreign exchange, given the huge assets of foreigners in China and the weak confidence of the Chinese people, foreign exchange reserves can be completely lost in an instant. Therefore, it is absolutely necessary to implement foreign exchange controls immediately after the outbreak of war. This measure can also indirectly curb the bank run on ordinary banks. If foreign exchange is restricted, people cannot purchase foreign exchange after withdrawing deposits, and what they withdraw is all legal tender, not cash, which cannot be used for hoarding. The bank run can naturally be indirectly affected and its momentum slightly curbed.

The above measures are only to passively control the chaotic situation, like using gravity to suppress the turbulent surface of the water so that its interior can be clarified. However, the closure of the exchanges, the suspension of debt payments, and the implementation of foreign exchange controls will inevitably result in the stagnation of economic activity. Wartime is precisely the time to exert national strength to fight for survival, and the stagnation of economic activity is an absolutely undesirable phenomenon. Because the stagnation of economic activity will make it impossible to exert national strength. Therefore, the next step is to implement proactive policies to promote the stagnant economic institutions, and this is our next step.

The next step can be discussed from five aspects: first, the government should use its strength to support credit institutions so that they can resume activity; second, the government should fully support industry and commerce so that they can adapt to the extraordinary environment of wartime; third, the government should use new credit to alleviate the deflationary situation after ordinary credit measures are lost in wartime; fourth, the government should fully suppress factors that disrupt the circulation of legal tender and ensure the circulation of legal tender; fifth, implement the mobilization of foreign debt to maintain foreign exchange stability. These are discussed separately as follows.

Since the banks have already been ordered to suspend payments, all debts are blocked. The longer the suspension lasts, the more overdue debt will accumulate. Under this kind of panic and contraction, it will be difficult to smoothly recover loans. If the government does not expand credit and directly provide assistance, the banks will have no day to reopen. In the money shop industry, there is usually no sufficient preparation for economic turnover, and they rely on interbank credit and short-term loans from banks. Since the banks are tightening credit at the top, and the money shops are on guard against each other, this method of credit transfer no longer exists, and it goes without saying that they cannot reopen. Banks and money shops are the hubs of economic activity. If they cannot resume activity, there is no hope of loosening the economic stagnation. Therefore, during the suspension of payments, the government should immediately provide substantial assistance to banks and money shops. The method can be divided into two points: first, the government can use the British method during the European War, entrusting the Big Three to directly loan to the banks, with the purpose of enabling each bank to meet its immediate debts. This measure is to enable each bank to settle its debts and resume business. Second, the Big Three should handle the discounting and rediscounting of various commercial bills with sufficient funds. The purpose of this measure is to enable the frozen funds of ordinary banks and money shops due to the suspension of payments to have room for activity. After the suspension of payments, the bills received by each company are frozen in an invisible manner. If the Big Three can substantially absorb these bills and replace them with their own credit, the frozen debts can continue to circulate, and the increase in active funds will greatly help to activate the market and settle debts. Britain also used this as one of its important measures during the war. The government directly advances money to the banks, and the frozen funds of bank bills can also be restored through the Big Three's full acceptance of discounting. The banks' active functions can gradually recover.

Second, the government should support the activities of industry and commerce. This point is very important, because industry and commerce are the source of materials in wartime, and all economic measures should aim to enable industry and commerce to fully exert their effectiveness. The activity of industry and commerce depends on funds. Some businesses are indeed operated by the government with its own funds, but private enterprises are still important. Regarding the working capital issue of private enterprises, we advocate that the government should follow the British method during the European War and directly guarantee the industrial and commercial loans of banks and money shops. In wartime, the political situation is uncertain, and even if banks and money shops have sufficient funds, they may not dare to lend them out as much as possible. This is probably unavoidable. If the government can directly provide credit guarantees so that banks and money shops can release funds without the risk of freezing, bank funds can be directly used to support production. This measure is also to enable the government's credit assistance to the financial sector to extend its effect to industry and commerce. Otherwise, even if the government rescues the financial sector, the financial sector will not dare to rescue industry and commerce, and the government's credit assistance to the financial sector will be meaningless. To enable the financial sector to fully utilize the credit granted by the government to support industry and commerce, it is absolutely necessary for the government to provide credit guarantees to the industrial sector.

Third, the government should prepare to use new credit to alleviate the shortage of small change at the beginning of the war. This point is also very important for our country. Because our currency organization is very complicated. After the implementation of the legal tender policy, although cash cannot be circulated legally, some of it is still scattered among the people. In some places, real money still occupies a dominant position. Once a credit crisis occurs, silver coins will be completely hoarded, and even general copper coins will disappear. It is expected that some unscrupulous merchants will transport currency to the inland to purchase copper coins and real money. The fact that Wuhan concentrated cash in the 16th year of the Republic of China can be used as a reference. Real money was quickly hoarded, small change was lacking, transactions were hindered, and some places even became dead markets. It is absolutely necessary to use new credit to stabilize the market. During the European War, Britain, France, and Germany all issued a large number of small-denomination banknotes at the beginning of the war, with the purpose of facilitating market financing and avoiding the stagnation of economic turnover. This point should be adopted by us. Moreover, after the outbreak of war, economic activity will inevitably shift to the interior. In the inland areas, small-denomination credit small change is especially necessary to cope with this extraordinary situation.

Fourth, sanction factors that disrupt the value of legal tender and ensure the circulation of legal tender. This point is also particularly important in our country. This can be discussed from the following points: first, the issue of the secret circulation of cash. The concentration of cash in our country has not been completely completed. Once a war breaks out, it will first be hoarded and disappear from the market, and even copper coins cannot be exchanged; then it will appear on the black market, becoming a powerful factor in undermining the circulation of legal tender. Because the cash of the people cannot be hoarded forever, after a considerable period of time, it will inevitably appear on the market, and black market transactions will arise from this. The United States during the Civil War and Europe during the European War all had similar experiences. Even in countries with developed credit systems, such as Britain, the secret circulation of silver coins cannot be explicitly prohibited. The experience of the disturbance of prices and harm to the circulation of legal tender after the emergence of cash on the black market after Wuhan concentrated cash in the 16th year of the Republic of China is also a lesson for us. Therefore, preventing cash and real money from appearing on the black market is a necessary measure to consolidate the circulation of legal tender. Second, the issue of using foreign exchange as a means of payment. During the currency panic in various countries during the European War, the use of foreign exchange for transactions became a common practice. As a result, foreign exchange soared due to increased demand, and local paper money became useless due to lack of use. During the period when Wuhan concentrated cash in the 16th year of the Republic of China, merchants competed to use Shanghai exchange and Shanghai banknotes as payment tools. As a result, Shanghai exchange soared to over 6,000 taels in a short period of time, and Wuhan regarded Central Bank notes as semi-legal tender and fell to the point where they could not be circulated in a short period of time. This historical fact deserves our attention. Prohibiting foreign exchange as a means of payment is probably a necessary method to consolidate the circulation of legal tender.

Fifth, concentrate debt and maintain foreign exchange stability. This point is extremely important and extremely difficult. Since foreign exchange controls have been implemented, foreign exchange cannot be locked up for a long time and will eventually be gradually opened up. How to maintain stability after opening up is our problem. During the European War, various countries successively implemented the mobilization of foreign debt to cope with foreign exchange. First, the state organized banks to try to buy it, then levied special taxes to force the people to hand it over voluntarily, and finally, it became a common practice to forcibly concentrate all foreign debt and sell it abroad by the government. Forcible concentration of foreign debt is probably an absolutely necessary measure for us. Judging from the effectiveness of our people, the people will never voluntarily offer it unless it is enforced. However, it is extremely difficult to stabilize foreign exchange with the strength of one country in wartime. The key point is to obtain international cooperation, but the forcible concentration of foreign debt is still one of the decisive measures we should take.

The main purpose of the above five points is to sanction disruptive factors in a passive way, and to support the activities of credit institutions with the power of the government in an active way, so as to achieve the goal of exerting national strength in wartime. The main point is the latter. There are still many other problems, and what is described here is only the main points. Finally, let us discuss the preparatory work that should be done before the war.

There are three points that we want to propose: first, cash in the hands of the people should be concentrated as soon as possible; second, the supply sources of currency should be unified as soon as possible; third, financial institutions should be adjusted as soon as possible. It cannot be denied that cash has not been completely concentrated. Once a war breaks out, the cash remaining in the hands of the people is expected to become a powerful factor in disrupting the market. In order to prevent the occurrence of black market transactions and the disruption of prices, cash concentration is absolutely necessary. Second, the unification of currency supply sources probably means the centralization of issuance. The banknotes in the market are still very complicated, and the banknotes of local banks still have a certain status in the interior. Once a war breaks out, due to the psychological effects of the people, price differences will inevitably occur in the market, and prices will be disrupted as a result. In order to prevent the emergence of this situation of price differences due to currency differences, the first step is to completely unify currency issuance. Once the currency is unified, there is no room for comparison or choice, and there will be no price differences. Third, the adjustment of financial institutions is even more important at present, and the problem is also very complicated. We only want to propose three points: first, the Central Bank system in the form of a joint venture of the Big Three is definitely not suitable for the extraordinary situation of wartime. The central agency for controlling finance should be organized and established as soon as possible. Second, the current bank organization with numerous small banks is definitely not suitable for the extraordinary situation of wartime. How to promote its concentration and merger is a problem that should be studied at present. Third, after the outbreak of war, the position of Shanghai will probably be difficult to determine. How to enable the government to choose the right financial path for the whole country after leaving Shanghai is one of the most noteworthy issues at present. These three points are the central issues for adjusting the banking system, and I hope to present them for consideration by domestic talents.

Evaluation of Chinese Hui Societies 193

— Bu Yu Zhi

Before entering the topic, three points should be clarified:

The scope of this article is only to analyze and evaluate the "facts" of Hui societies. Opinions on papers and writings on Hui societies will not be involved unless absolutely necessary.

The author has lived abroad for many years and has not been able to personally investigate the recent trends of Hui societies in China. The recent descriptions of the Hui society system have also not been read one by one. The materials in this article are only based on known writings.

Due to limited space, the various methods of Hui societies cannot be explained in detail. Here, I would like to introduce two monographs for readers' reference.

A. Wang Zongpei's "Hui Societies of China," published by the Shanghai China Cooperative Society in 1931.

B. Yang Ximeng's "A Study of Chinese Hui Societies" (Collection No. 1 of the Institute of Social Sciences, National Central Research Institute), published by the Commercial Press in 1925.

I. Importance of "Hui Societies" in China and Abroad

Starting from the early years of the Republic of China, when Mr. Xue Xiangzhou and a few friends advocated the German Schulze-Delitzsch cooperative banking system, and in 1919 founded the "Shanghai National Cooperative Savings Bank," and in 1920 published the "Common People's Weekly" to promote cooperative theory, this was the beginning of cooperative theory and movement in China.

In 1921, a major drought spread across five northern provinces, and the fields were full of corpses. Chinese and foreign talents tried to provide relief. After the disaster relief in 1921, there was still more than two or three million yuan left. Therefore, in 1922, the "China-Foreign Joint Relief and Disaster Relief General Association" was established. This was the hub of the rural credit cooperation movement in China.

In 1928, Jiangsu Province established a farmers' bank and also established a "Cooperative Guidance Staff Training Institute," which also made important contributions to the credit cooperation movement. In addition, there were also individuals and groups who either engaged in translation and writing (such as Mr. Lou Tongsun Zishu De), or conducted theoretical research and reference experiments (such as the Shanghai China Cooperative Society). The number was very large. In 1931, the Ministry of Industry further formulated the "Provisional Regulations for Rural Cooperation."

In this cooperative movement, an event was linked and aroused, which was very important, that is, the attention of a group of people to an old system in China—Hui societies. In a few years, articles on Hui societies were often seen in several important magazines published in Shanghai, Peiping, Hangzhou, etc. In 1931, Wang Zongpei even published a book titled "Hui Societies of China," which was the beginning of monographs on Hui societies in China. Today, the Commercial Press has recently published a new book titled "Research on Chinese Hui Societies," which also contributes a lot of materials.

From the surface, Hui societies are just a small game among the people. In a few years, there have been so many papers and two monographs, which seems to be making a fuss over a trifle. However, from the perspective of the role, efficiency, and impact of Hui societies, it seems that Chinese people have paid too little attention to it.

As far as the author knows, 157 years ago (1778 AD, the 43rd year of Qianlong), the French missionaries in Beijing wrote "Memoires Ccocenant les Chinese," and its 16th volume (pages 384-387) described the system of Chinese Hui societies. Also, 55 years ago (1880 AD, the 6th year of Guangxu), Father Lebouca, who had lived in China for a long time, wrote "Asscciaons de la Chine," which introduced Hui societies (pages 108-125) in more detail; and praised the simple method and strong friendship of Hui societies. Also, 44 years ago (1891 AD, the 17th year of Guangxu), Simon, who had served as a consul in China for a long time and understood and loved China very much, wrote "La Cite chinoisse," which introduced Hui societies in more detail, and attached seven diagrams at the end of the book to illustrate various Hui styles, believing that Hui societies were a wonderful product of mutual assistance among the people.

After the opening of the University of Paris, Professor of Economics Simiand instructed the author to give a lecture on Hui societies. During the lecture, teachers and students discussed it for a long time. Among the questions, the three that deserve our attention the most are:

Has the origin of Hui societies been solved? The author's answer is that the origin has not been solved, but based on reasonable speculation, it has at least a thousand years of history. (According to Wang's book and the author's speculation, it has been more than a thousand years)

Why are Hui societies so popular in China, but there are no explicit regulations in Chinese legislation? The answer is: Chinese society values morality over law, which is the opposite of Western society, and cites Confucius's "Lead them with virtue, regulate them with propriety, and they will have a sense of shame and moreover be reformed; lead them with government regulations and restrain them with penalties, and the people will avoid wrong-doing but will have no sense of shame" as the basis. It also cites the views of Professor Mauss of the French Academy of Social Sciences: "Eastern countries" are ruled by moral customs; Western countries are ruled by law (see his outline of sociology described in "Annales Sociologigues" 1934 Paris Alcan)

Hui societies are so popular in China and so effective. How many Hui society groups are there each year? How many people participate? How much is borrowed from Hui societies? Is the purpose of Hui societies more for production or for consumption? If it is more for consumption, what kind of consumption is more? China does not have statistics on the above points? In addition to answering with speculation, the author can only say that China does not yet have statistics.

As for the contribution of the Hui society system to modern culture, everyone undoubtedly affirmed two points:

Contribution to the "History of Cooperation": Economists believe that credit cooperation is a modern thing. If Hui societies are recognized as a kind of borrowing cooperation, then this conclusion should be broken.

Contribution to the "Cooperative System": Although cooperationism has been advocated by scholars, supported by the government, and promoted by political parties, it is now inevitably declining. The failure of cooperative societies is often heard. As for the Hui society system, scholars do not pay attention to it, and the government does not ask about it, but it can naturally circulate among the people for thousands of years. There must be its characteristics in this. This feature can undoubtedly contribute to cooperativists.

Regarding the three questions about Hui societies: the origin of Hui societies, whether Hui societies should have a legislative basis, and the statistics of Hui societies, the author does not list them again, but hopes that we can conduct further research and discussion to resolve the doubts of some people.

As for the characteristics of Hui societies, we cannot deny the fact. Several years ago, regarding Hui societies, many people in China advocated changing Hui societies to cooperation. The author talked to several professors at the University of Paris, and they also advocated changing cooperation to Hui societies. In the future, will it be "cooperationizing Hui societies, or will it be Hui societyizing cooperation"? This is a question worth discussing by everyone.

If everyone can finish reading this article and understand the value of Hui societies, I think this question will not be difficult to solve. (To be continued)

Investigation: Overview of Tea Exports in April 204

According to a report from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, tea exports in April that passed inspection and were approved for export totaled 3,172.53 metric tons, a decrease of 12,394.58 metric tons compared to the same month last year. It is noted that this month is the beginning of the new tea season, and normally inland tea merchants would transport large quantities of new tea to Shanghai to compete for sales overseas. However, recently, local tea warehouses have suspended trading and closed down in opposition to the unified control of tea transportation and sales in Anhui and Jiangxi, resulting in new tea being held up in the producing areas and unable to be transported, and the local tea market is in a state of stagnation. Therefore, the quantity of exports has decreased significantly. The following is a table showing the statistics of tea exports by country in April:

What is the Point of Being a League of Nations Councilor? 214

— Useless

The League of Nations was originally a paper tiger, a tool for several powerful nations to manipulate and control weaker nations. Therefore, after the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident), this paper tiger was already exposed. With the Abyssinian Crisis (Second Italo-Ethiopian War), this paper tiger can be considered to have ceased to exist. Therefore, the seat of a councilor in the League of Nations now, let alone campaigning or requesting for it, even if they sent an invitation with twenty-four pages, one could only respond with the four characters "Respectfully decline".

Since the establishment of the League of Nations, our country's representatives have strived for a councilor seat in the League of Nations Administrative Council, but it was never resolved. Ultimately, due to China's weak military strength and many domestic troubles, they were disappointed. This year in September, the League of Nations Administrative Council will be reorganized again. The Administrative Council Organization Committee has recently discussed the allocation of councilor seats. According to the committee's resolution, this year's League of Nations General Assembly should add one non-permanent councilor seat to the Administrative Council to appease China. Although the committee's decision still awaits the approval of the Administrative Council and a two-thirds vote by the General Assembly, judging from today's trends, China's acquisition of a seat on the Administrative Council this year does not seem to face much difficulty. Although this matter is appreciated as a gesture of goodwill from the League of Nations Administrative Council Organization Committee, and we are grateful for their attention, at this stage, there is no need to go to the League of Nations to serve as a non-permanent councilor. Let me ask, what is it like to be a non-permanent councilor of the League of Nations Administrative Council? What is it like not to be a non-permanent councilor of the League of Nations Administrative Council?

I will now briefly review the League of Nations' political achievements over the past few years and the current situation of the League of Nations member states, and consider them. The current organizational system of the League of Nations Administrative Council was actually established with the formation of the Locarno Treaties in 1926, when Germany joined the League of Nations. At that time, it was decided that Britain, France, Italy, Japan, and Germany would be permanent councilors, with nine additional non-permanent councilors. Therefore, the League of Nations' organization was entirely centered on Britain, France, Italy, Japan, and Germany. Now, Germany and Japan have withdrawn from the League of Nations. Although Italy has not withdrawn, since the League of Nations resolved that Italy was an aggressor nation, the League of Nations has adopted an opposing stance towards Italy. Therefore, although Italy's name has not been withdrawn, it has de facto seceded. Therefore, the current League of Nations has only Britain and France as its center, as well as Soviet Russia, which joined later. However, Britain and France have different dreams in the same bed, and their opinions also differ. Therefore, there is also talk of Britain withdrawing from the League of Nations. To join such a disorganized League of Nations is truly foolish.

Moreover, the reason why countries want to join the League of Nations is because it can help weak countries and use the power of the League of Nations to sanction the aggression of strong countries, and use the League of Nations as a relief agency for weak nations. However, during the September 18th Incident, although our country sought divination and prayed sincerely, there was no effect. During the Abyssinian Crisis, Abyssinia also shouted itself hoarse and prostrated in prayer. Although the League of Nations performed great feats, Abyssinia was eventually annihilated, and the effect was also equal to zero. And the membership fees that the League of Nations member states pay to the League of Nations are not insignificant. Only a big fool would be willing to waste this kind of wronged money. Therefore, judging from the above situation, even being a member state of the League of Nations is somewhat disdainful, and wanting to be a non-permanent councilor is even more futile.

— Zou Heng

The next room was the pharmacy, with rows and rows of white-painted shelves filled with medicine bottles of various sizes. "He went to little Zhang's room again." Miss Li glanced at him.

"Are we taking appointments today or not? He didn't tell me."

Sending a Letter 216

— Li Xuan

Old Scar sat at the entrance of the temple, his back, covered in a layer of mud, bare. The temple front was still and quiet. Sunlight shone on the facing wall all the way to the offering table of the Five Path Lord statue. Old Scar leaned against the base of the wall, using a greasy black hand to scratch the ribs under his armpit. His fingernails rasped, and small flakes of mud fell down like bran. He yawned, lowered his head, and began to catch lice on the faded, patchwork military jacket again. The lice were wriggling along the torn seams, white ones, with a small, dark red sac inside their small, plump bodies. He watched the little things scurrying about, trying to hide, and smiled, revealing his blackened lips:

"Where do you think you're going!"

He gently pinched one between two fingers, rubbing it. After a while, the louse fainted. He threw it onto the brick under his feet and pressed down with his thumbnail. *Pop*, a slight sound rang out. Old Scar licked his lips and joked to himself:

"Come back and bite me next life, ha."

There were so many lice. As soon as he crushed one, he turned around to find two more piled together. Old Scar smiled slightly. He opened his palm and spat a mouthful of sticky phlegm into it. He rubbed his hands together and then, like a crab, spread out his arms. He spread his thumb and forefinger on each hand and pinched a louse, separating them.

"Why are you two being so intimate in broad daylight!"

"Lice that can't be gotten rid of, thieves that can't be caught—Ah, I should go find something to eat."

torn blue woolen pants, her hair was disheveled and draped around her neck. She ran unsteadily like an old woman, holding a little girl in her arms. "We're a foreign firm, what are we afraid of."

He thought that this spring marked four years since the Chinese soldiers were defeated that year, and he hadn't seen them since. But there were more and more soldiers walking like ducks.

Camellia 218

— Ai Tu

"In April, the holly blooms with camellias,

Young girls climb all over the mountains,

Could there be a young lad coming from somewhere,

With a handsome face,

Singing mountain songs drifting in the wind,

Singing makes the young girls' chests jump!

Picking camellias, not wanting too few,

The young girls' wages are given to the mountain song lad..."

Gui Zhen's tattered blue cloth clothes carried a light cloth bag. Her youthful, rosy cheeks faced the sun. The April sun, like her face, climbed up the hillside with a bit of shyness. The distant, spreading hillside! Covered with verdant camellias, reflecting a silent picture in their eyes. This group of young girls climbed up the hillside one after another. Most of them sang gentle and charming mountain songs. Gui Zhen jumped innocently, shaking her head, and her black braid fluttered in the spring breeze. Just then, a stone was thrown from under the thick leaves of the small tree, followed by chuckles. Gui Zhen's heart jumped. She opened her eyes and looked over:

"It's that foul-mouthed Xiao Zhen!" She cursed, jumping and running over. "When did you come?"

The young girl, Xiao Zhen, did not answer her, but just couldn't help laughing for a while before saying from the thick leaves:

"Don't run over! Guess what else is here? Your mountain song lad is waiting for you!"

Gui Zhen's face turned red, like the sun hanging in the eastern sky.

"Sing! Sister Gui Zhen! Your singing is even better than the lad's."

"Hmph! You really know how to tease people. You're actually mixed up with the young lad! Still trying to spread rumors!"

Gui Zhen said, laughing, and grabbed their arms, her happy heart leaping, and ran to the hillside. It was the Qingming Festival. It had rained for a few days, and the dry wilderness was now covered with moist dew. Camellias "sprouted green" all over the fields. The yellowish-purple and light green tea buds were all blooming, gently swaying in the gentle wind. From near and far, there were girls picking tea everywhere. Their bodies were so light, lively, and hopping like swallows. They stretched out their arms and started busy with the work of picking tea. Gui Zhen, Xiao Qi, and A Si, were also girls picking flowers in this tea mountain. So, as soon as they climbed the hillside, they could meet many acquaintances. Everyone sang, argued, and shouted together, but their hands were constantly picking, rarely taking the time to look at the distant hillside and the sun, which was gradually slipping away with its red and beautiful colors. But they were mostly young girls who loved to talk and laugh. Like Gui Zhen and Xiao Zhen, they kept talking and laughing. Sometimes, Gui Zhen secretly broke some dry branches and threw them into Xiao Zhen's bamboo basket, then, pressing the mouth of her own cloth bag with her left hand, laughed.

"Don't be so annoying! I'll tell your lover tonight that you've hooked up with someone else on the mountain!"

"Go ahead and say it! I don't have one, only you have a dozen or so, A Si! Are you right?"

A Si quickly picked the tender tea buds. Hearing them fooling around, she couldn't help but raise her head:

"Who knows, you all have ten or eight!"

Saying this, the three couldn't help but laugh.

"Okay! Xiao Zhen, pity her, that foul-mouthed girl has no man, give her three or two!"

"Always fooling around, look, other people have picked full baskets, only we have picked so little, how can we go back to face people!"

A Si said, twisting her mouth. She thought of home, of her old mother at home! Her weak old mother, she couldn't go up the mountain to pick tea anymore. So, besides her brother working as a farmhand in someone else's house, the family's expenses still depended on her tea picking income to help. But, although she had strength and could pick, she could only pick fifteen or sixteen catties at most (very few people could pick twenty catties). Each catty was only four copper coins, and picking all day long was only a hundred copper coins!………………Thinking about it, she became anxious again.

"It's really not easy!" A Si muttered: "Look! This year's spring is too cold, most of the camellias are frozen and withered. Qingming has arrived, and although it has rained for a few days, there are still many that have not sprouted!"

"Really! If you look at it this way! In three or five days of picking, there will be nothing to pick! Then we won't have any work to do!"

Gui Zhen said in a depressed tone, raising her head to look at the green tea trees all over the fields, and the girls picking tea all over the fields. The sun was already hanging high in the sky. She also thought of the low tea prices last year and the sluggish sales:

"Maybe, this year will be the same, with no sales! I heard that the seas, Shanghai, are full of Japanese goods."

They talked and searched, looking at the tea hills that were not full of tender buds. The sun was about to set.

Continued on Page 5 of the Local Supplement

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

It was going down. However, they were hungry, enduring their sore waists, and picking tea leaves nervously.

"Sister Gui Zhen, I heard that picking at the Liu family's is only three copper coins a catty, and that scale is very big too!"

Xiao Qi shook her head. A Si continued:

"The harvest is bad, and there are no sales, it's even harder for us tea pickers!"

In Gui Zhen's mind, she thought of tomorrow, the day after tomorrow, maybe there would be no tea to pick, no wages…… She raised her head and looked at them, sighed, and said:

"The sun is setting, it's going to get dark! Let's go back!"

As they walked arm in arm, following the many girls, in twos and threes, running down the dark hillside, the clear mountain songs, followed by the spring evening wind, gently wafted:

"The sun sets in the west, a bit of yellow,

Young lady carries a stick and chases a weasel.

The weasel's feet are small and can steal chickens;

The young lady's feet are small and can steal a man."

Hu Zhangzhao's "Analects"

Traffic (1300) 9:30 PM to 10:00 PM

Zigong said, "To be poor without flattery, and rich without arrogance, what do you think?" The Master said, "Acceptable, but not as good as being poor and joyful, and rich and loving propriety." Zigong said, "The Book of Odes says, 'As if cutting, as if filing; as if carving, as if polishing.' Is that what it means?" The Master said, "Ci, now I can discuss the Book of Odes with you. Tell you the past and you know the future."

The Master said, "Do not worry that others do not know you; worry that you do not know others."

The Master said, "Governing with virtue is like the North Star, abiding in its place, and all the stars revolve around it."

The Master said, "The three hundred Odes can be summed up in one sentence: 'Do not think impurely.'"

The Master said, "Lead them with government orders and regulate them with punishments, and the people will avoid [crime] but have no sense of shame. Lead them with virtue and regulate them with ritual, and they will have shame and also be upright."

Pingtan (Storytelling and Ballad Singing) 221

He Yunfang and He Qinfang's "Double Pearl Phoenix"

Central West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter: "Wulong Temple"

The weather is clear and the herbs are fragrant. Unable to dispel my worries, I stroll through the streets. I am, born with a chivalrous heart that is hard to subdue. Unexpectedly, I married Yan Xijiao. I have to swallow my anger and suffer in silence. Unexpected incidents are no one's concern. Affairs of the pillow are especially strange. She is, like a drifting catkin, hard to restrain. Constantly, stirring up trouble, looking for snakes in the grass. Oh, how hateful! Oh, how hateful! Her dissolute behavior is not punished by heaven. Now, her disloyal heart has already been revealed. Oh, Yan Xijiao, I see that, your constant quarrels are not without reason. When the truth is revealed, how will you resist? Full of thoughts, my mind is confused. I meet her mother on the street. She has failed the fragrant quilt until today. How can I comfort Xijiao? She is, tears often thinking of you. I still regret my troubles. You must know that, quarrels between husband and wife are common. You should not, stubbornly run elsewhere. It is so coincidental to meet here. I advise you to be patient and return to your fragrant nest for now. My thoughts are confused, and my body is too lazy to lift. I am, suddenly startled by a shout. One is, a thorn in my eye, meeting with resentment in my heart. The other is, afraid she will not come even in broad daylight. But they say Sanlang is sitting downstairs, making me suspicious. This time, I will punish his unfaithfulness. I will make him, kneel in the courtyard to apologize. Only then can I quell my anger.

Opening Chapter: "Yutangchun"

Yutangchun, famous for her beautiful voice. Pure and clean, a girl with a noble spirit. Virtuous in nature, high in spirit. Singing poems and writing lyrics are her strengths. She loves, Jinlong, the son of a wealthy family. A talented man and beautiful woman, a good couple. A handsome Wang married to a beautiful woman. Appreciating the moon and watching flowers, a knowing friend. The only one who pities each other is Wang's family. In the end, the red silk is broken and suffers a disaster. Harm the slave, an evil reputation for killing her husband. The adulterer and adulteress plot cunningly. The bird is bound. Suffering in the three trials, with the body in agony. The original way, escorted to the east, covered in blood and mud. Reopen the case. Wang Jinlong has already won the top prize in the imperial examination. A beautiful wife who does not abandon her true identity. Su San confesses her grievances in detail. Scolding the unfaithful man in the hall. The case is judged, and the true culprit is caught. Movie News

Recent News from Tianyi 224

— Bai Yun

New Movie Release: Tianyi's latest sound production, "Flowers and Grass," passed yesterday (the 9th). Therefore, it is scheduled to be publicly screened at the Jincheng Theater after "New and Old Shanghai." It will be previewed in the morning for guests from all walks of life.

Script Submitted for Review: "Spring in a Water Country," written by Shao Zuiweng. The revised script was submitted to Beijing for review a few days ago.

Script Writing: Currently, Hong Shen is writing the script for "Floating Clouds" in Suzhou, which is expected to be completed before the 20th. Leng Bo is writing the scenes for "Peaceful Flowers." Zuo Ming is writing the script for "The Adventures of Mr. Wang": The preliminary review will be sent out within days.

Specially Commissioned Screenwriters: Tianyi plans to mass produce movies and needs many scripts. Therefore, it plans to specially commission several screenwriters. The candidates will be announced soon.

Short Film Production: The bouncing drama of the hibiscus flower is extremely popular in Shanghai. Its masterpiece, "Du Shiniang," has been captured by Tianyi on film.

Personnel Changes: Ye Qianyu has joined Tianyi as the film supervisor for "Mr. Wang." Zuo Ming serves as screenwriter and director. Xu Wei has joined Tianyi as an art director. Xie Renmei has arrived in Shanghai from Singapore to assist.

Lon Chaney Jr.'s Demeanor in "Calling Dr. Death" 225

Nanjing Screening

"Incarnation Girl" Character Biographies 226

— Bai Shui

Yuan Meiyun: Plays Zhang Shouben, the "Incarnation Girl." Disguised as a man, her demeanor is brilliant. Sometimes a man, sometimes a woman, it is impossible to tell the difference. She gives an excellent performance.

Wang Yin: Plays Lin Songpo, a wealthy and amorous young man who is kind-hearted and affectionate. He shuttles between three young ladies: Yuan Meiyun, Zhou Xuan, and Xu Manli, with endless romance and inexhaustible pleasure.

Zhou Xuan: Plays the affectionate woman Zhu Naifang, skilled in coquetry and charm, pursuing Yuan Meiyun with all her might, resulting in countless jokes and interesting events. Her performance is sweet and honey-like, humorous and...

Han Langen: Plays Zhang Xuan, Yuan Meiyun's cousin. He is reckless, panicked, lacks the strength to truss a chicken, likes to cause trouble, is as greedy as a hungry cat, and has sticky fingers like a thief. He is a great treasure in "Incarnation Girl."

Xu Manli: Plays Li Airong, Wang Yin's lover, a serpentine metropolitan woman.

Jiang Xiu: Plays Zhang Yuanlun, Yuan Meiyun's father, who is also a wealthy overseas Chinese businessman. His performance is extremely calm and impeccable.

Wang Guilin: Plays Zhang Rongweng, Yuan Meiyun's grandfather, a loving old man. His performance is excellent.

Cang Yinqiu: Plays the female student Wang Manli, a silly girl who is a good friend of Han Langen.

Qin Tong: Plays Zhang Zhaohuan, Zhang Guilin's nephew, a busy man in "Incarnation Girl."

Hongda: Plays Li Si, a servant in the Zhang family, who is foolish and dull-witted.
